Han said that the train would arrive in Wande tonight, visit the Lingyan Temple tomorrow morning, and give a speech to various agencies in Tai'an in the afternoon. Due to time constraints, he might not be able to visit Mr. Feng. After visiting Qufu from Tai'an, the bank presidents and General Commander Shi (Yousan) would return to Jinan. He would then go to Yanzhou for inspection, then to Jining, and take a car to the counties under Caozhou, which would take about ten days before returning to Jinan, after which he would go to Beiping. Han then instructed Jinan Mayor Wen Chenglie that the recent heavy rains would cause the Yellow River to rise, and the dikes might be in danger. He should make preparations and order the River Affairs Bureau to prepare 50,000 sacks. During the rescue, filling them with earth to dam the dikes would be more effective than straw. Wen replied in agreement. At 10:50, Shi Yousan arrived at the station, and the train departed south. Han's train was the Beiping armored train, engine number 315, with four passenger cars, three flat cars, twelve armored cars, and six iron boxcars, totaling 26 cars. It carried three long-distance buses and two sedan cars. Meng Xiande, the captain of the Beiping armored train, accompanied him. After Han's inspection, the seal of the commander-in-chief was handed over to Sun Tongxuan, the commander of the 20th Division, to act on his behalf. However, Sun was inspecting the troops in Jiaodong. Before Sun returned, Cao Fulin, the commander of the 29th Division, acted on his behalf, assisted by Liu Shuxiang, the chief of staff of the General Headquarters. The chairman's seal was handed over to Li Shuchun, the director of the Department of Civil Affairs, to act on his behalf, assisted by Zhang Shaotang, the secretary-general of the Provincial Government. All military and political agencies were notified to comply. (10th)

Jiang Dingwen

Military Headquarters Moves to Bengbu 77

Jiang Arrives in Bengbu to Assume the Post of Garrison Commander

Bengbu Dispatch: Jiang Dingwen, the commander of the Second Army, was ordered by the Military Commission to serve as the garrison commander of Bengbu. His military headquarters moved here from Xuzhou on the 8th. Jiang went to Zhengzhou from Kaifeng to attend the dedication ceremony of the Second Army Martyrs Cemetery. He then arrived in Bengbu via Xuzhou at 2:30 this morning (10th). After getting off the train, Jiang took a car to the military headquarters (Chamber of Commerce) and assumed his new position as the garrison commander of Bengbu that day. This morning, the reporter went to interview him. According to him, the Military Commission considered the situation in Bengbu to be relatively complicated. At a time when the campaign to suppress the bandits in western Anhui was in full swing, this area urgently needed to strengthen its garrison. The Xu division of our army has made progress in suppressing the bandits in the direction of Huoqiu. The bandits have been cleared east of the Pi River. The area west of the Pi River is still being cleared. Since I have assumed the position of Bengbu garrison commander, I should do my best to consolidate the defense for the local security responsibility, and so on. Currently, the defense here is the responsibility of the Li Brigade of the Ninth Division of the Jiang Department. Jiang will gather the officers and soldiers of his troops for a speech within a few days, and convene the heads of the various units and military officers stationed in Bengbu to hold a garrison meeting to discuss the security matters related to maintaining law and order. The military headquarters and garrison headquarters of the Second Army are still temporarily located in the Chamber of Commerce. As soon as Chen Tiaoyuan's First Route Army Headquarters leaves Bengbu, it will move to the old site of Fengyangg关. It is reported that the First Route Army Headquarters has decided to move to Huaiyin County, Jiangsu, and personnel and soldiers from various places are preparing to depart within a few days. (January 10)

The Jiangsu Provincial Government Accepts

Chamber of Commerce Decides on Business Tax Rate 78

Provincial Government Only Needs Annual Tax Revenue of Six Million

In order to solve the financial problems of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce specially convened a meeting of all executive and supervisory committee members in the province. After several days of discussion, it was finally decided to approve the Jiangsu Provincial Government's proposal to reorganize the business tax, stop implementing other commercial taxes. The business tax rate standard, except for those originally levied at 5 per mille or more, will still be levied as before. Those originally levied at 1 per mille will be changed to 2 per mille, those originally levied at 2 per mille will be changed to 4 per mille. Cotton and silkworm cocoons will be reduced by 1 per mille. Gold and silver jewelry will be taxed based on the amount of capital. It will be implemented from the autumn of the 21st year. Tax payments will be prepaid at the beginning of each quarter. If a store closes down midway, it will be refunded on a daily basis. Furthermore, meetings will be convened by the old prefectural district to announce the constitutional decree to assist government offices in collecting taxes, and to advise merchants to comply with regulations and pay taxes. The above measures were negotiated with the provincial departments by the standing committee members of the association, including Yu Xiaochuan, Wang Jingting, Shi Junqing, and Lan Bohua. The provincial side stated that it could be accepted as long as the annual tax revenue reached six million yuan. As to whether the first quarter after the start of the reorganization should be taken as the standard, the association, in order to tighten the expenditure of the tax bureaus in various counties, also suggested to the provincial departments to appropriately abolish the business tax bureaus in various counties, and the collection matters should be handled by a section set up by the Finance Bureau. Counties without a Finance Bureau can be handled by the county government on its behalf. The provincial side quite agreed with this. (11th)

The Jiangsu Provincial Government Hosts Members of the Chamber of Commerce

Reports on the Progress of Planning Provincial Finances

The Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce has been holding meetings for days to discuss commercial tax measures. The provincial government specially hosted the members of the association at the provincial government at noon on the 8th, and held talks after the meal. Chairman Gu first expressed his welcome, and detailed the actual situation of the provincial finances, expressing his deep gratitude to the business community for assisting the government in solving the compensation methods. Subsequently, Director Shu, Yu Xiaochuan, Shi Junqing, Wu Minyu, Zhu Dexuan, and others from the Chamber of Commerce successively expressed their opinions. It was dismissed at 3 pm. The following is a record of Chairman Gu's speech:

(Gentlemen of the Chamber of Commerce, I recently gathered in Zhenjiang to discuss commercial tax issues. I would like to take this opportunity to invite you all to gather together. I am very pleased. You all have a deep understanding of Jiangsu's politics, and you have a thorough understanding of the financial situation and the principles of commercial tax. At the same time, you are very sincere in seeking assistance in tax collection, which is especially gratifying to the provincial government.

Jiangsu's finances, during the tenure of the former Director Zhang Yongni, had not yet determined a budget. At that time, the total annual expenditure was about 17 million yuan. By the time the budget for the 19th year was established, the annual expenditure was about 24 million yuan. At the end of the year, the resulting revenue was about 7 million yuan short. For the 20th year's budget expenditure, it increased to more than 26 million yuan. Comparing revenue and expenditure, as of December of the 20th year, that is, the first half of the 20th year, it was already 12 million yuan short. It is estimated that by the end of the year, the shortfall will be more than 20 million yuan. We came to serve in Jiangsu at the end of the 20th year. At that time, we already felt the exhaustion of the financial future. At the same time, we examined the income for the 21st year. The only reliable item was the land tax, and other miscellaneous income. The total for the whole year was only more than 7 million yuan. Among them, after deducting various loans for dike construction and military advances, the net balance was only more than 3 million yuan. Compared with the actual expenditure during the era of the former Director Zhang, this small amount of revenue is still 14 million yuan short. Compared with the 19th and 20th years, the difference is even greater, making it impossible to establish a budget for the 21st year. Jiangsu's political affairs will be in a state of stagnation. If the government does not ask whether the source of income is reliable, and simply assumes that the income items are forcibly suitable, the resulting income will only be like a painted cake, while the expenditure must be paid in full. It is inevitable to borrow from the future to make up for the present, with thousands of holes. It is still unavoidable to repeat the mistakes of virtual revenue and actual expenditure in the past, repeating the same old story. Jiangsu's financial bankruptcy will be in a position of eternal doom, which is by no means what those who value the facts believe.

Financial methods are nothing more than two kinds: increasing revenue and reducing expenditure. First, start with reducing expenditure. The government has already strictly implemented austerity. In the current situation, it is really impossible to reduce any more. However, even this current situation cannot have enough income to maintain it. As for the method of increasing revenue, after the abolition of the likin, the annual revenue has suddenly lacked a huge amount, and no method of compensation has been raised so far. Our country is an industrially immature country, and the government's source of income is nothing more than agriculture and commerce. The burden of Jiangsu's land tax surcharge is the heaviest in other provinces. If the burden is increased again, the rural areas will be bankrupt. This is what the people of Jiangsu commonly recognize. As for reorganizing the land tax to seek increased income, it cannot be effective in a short period of time. In terms of commerce, the business tax is the largest item. The previous performance in this province is well known to the people of the whole province. In terms of reorganization, if we rely solely on any method of the government, it is difficult to hope for a quick effect. Since income cannot be increased dramatically, and expenditure is difficult to reduce any further, the finances for the 20th year have actually fallen into a desperate situation. The economy is the mother of everything. Since the finances have fallen into a desperate situation, then Jiangsu's political affairs will be paralyzed in every way. We Jiangsu people are responsible for governing Jiangsu. Not only can we not seek positive development, but we cannot even plan negative maintenance. We are deeply concerned about the future, and we are all deeply self-reproachful. After thinking again and again, in order to avoid the stagnation of political affairs, we have no choice but to reluctantly seek to remedy the insufficient portion of this year's income. It is estimated that the insufficient amount, in addition to seeking assistance from the central government and raising other methods, can obtain about 5 to 6 million, and there is still a difference of 6 million yuan. This difference can only be met by two methods: opening up new taxes or reorganizing old taxes. Opening up new taxes, no matter what method is used, will inevitably increase the burden on the people. The people of Jiangsu are declining, and it is difficult to bear. Moreover, we are unwilling to do so. This is well known to the provincial government. As for reorganizing the existing business tax, the past effects have been as described above. If we start reorganizing, if there are no special methods, we are still worried that it will not be effective in the shortest time. When the need is urgent, and the difference in quantity is so great, in order to urgently seek compensation, we have no choice but to take effective methods. Therefore, we have the plan to try out a special business tax. We know that the nature of this tax law is similar to the likin, and we are afraid that there will be abuses in the future. Therefore, after repeated consideration, and after detailed consultation with the central government, the reason why we have not immediately started is that we are also working hard to find a proper solution, seeking a win-win situation. Now that you all believe that the government and businesses should cooperate closely to urgently reorganize the business tax, and that the annual income is expected to reach 6 million yuan, the government only asks that it can meet the required amount and establish a budget. There is no fixed and unchangeable prejudice. Since you are willing to be responsible for assisting as much as possible, in order to have a dramatic increase in business tax revenue, we can abandon the original proposal to handle special business tax. In addition to the business tax rate and reorganization methods being properly planned and handled by the Department of Finance, we hope that you will uphold your original intention of assisting the government, and do your great strength to persuade and support, so that it becomes a correct and reliable income. However, after this business tax has been reorganized, if the result of the first quarter's income can reach 1.1 million yuan, then the annual income can be inferred from this, and the income budget can have a considerable percentage. In case the income number cannot be as we predicted, we will still have to rely on you to continue to assist and continue to find ways to compensate in order to maintain the budget for the 21st year, so as not to cause Jiangsu's political affairs to fall into a state of stagnation. This is the concern of the entire political life of Jiangsu. Not only is it the private concern of I and my colleagues. Today I hastily invited you, and the hospitality is simple and crude. I am very sorry. Please give me more guidance. I look forward to it very much.

Director Shu reported on the financial situation, and stated the reasons for the proposed special business tax, and the methods for reorganizing the business tax in the future. The general idea is the same as what Chairman Gu said.

Zhejiang Province Determines Provisional Measures for the Collection of Business Tax 79

Various Industries Have Expressed Agreement

Hangzhou News: The business tax rate in Zhejiang Province has been revised again, reducing by one-half according to the new rate promulgated last month. It will be announced and implemented in the coming days. The Hangzhou City Chamber of Commerce specially convened a joint meeting of the standing committee members of various industry associations and the executive and supervisory committee members of this association this afternoon (11th). More than 50 people attended. Chairman Wang Zhuzhai first reported on the general situation of the association and the provincial chamber of commerce requesting to exempt the increase of business tax to 10 per mille. Then, Xu Xinggong reported on the process of the provincial chamber of commerce publicly recommending representatives to petition, organizing a special committee, and party, government, and business tea parties, and the results obtained now, which was very detailed. He also reported the four provisional measures for the collection of business tax in Zhejiang Province passed by the provincial government's political affairs meeting. Finally, he said that if you have any opinions on these provisional measures, please express them immediately for detailed discussion. Then, Zhou Shiluo of the new medicine industry, Yu Shaoyan of the Guanghuo industry, Li Jintang of the cloth industry, Yan Yunqiao of the clothing industry, and others successively expressed their approval. However, they asked the chairman to ask the officials to postpone the provisional measures until the autumn to start collecting. The chairman said that he would do his best to negotiate with the officials. Finally, a draft was drawn up to publish a notice to inform the various industries in the city to check and handle it, and the meeting was adjourned after it was passed.

Provisional Measures for the Collection of Business Tax in Zhejiang Province: (1) The business tax rates of various industries stipulated in Article 3 of the Regulations on the Collection of Business Tax in Zhejiang Province shall be temporarily applied to the provisions of these measures. (2) All industries that levy tax based on total business revenue or income shall change from 2 per mille to 5 per mille, from 5 per mille to 8 per mille, and those that levy 10 per mille shall remain unchanged. (3) All industries that levy tax based on the amount of capital shall change from 4 per mille to 5 per mille, from 5 per mille to 8 per mille, and those that levy 10 per mille shall remain unchanged. Those that levy 20 per mille shall be changed to 10 per mille. (4) For those in the goods sales industry that belong to whole selling, the tax rate stipulated in Item 2 of these measures shall be reduced by one-half.

Educational Turmoil Erupts in Jiangxi Province 89

Reaction to Chen Jianyou's Replacement of Principals

The undercurrent of education in Jiangxi Province erupted uncontrollably on the 8th after the announcement of the principals of provincial middle schools and above. The reaction was swift after the announcement was made. Education Director Chen Jianyou became the target of public criticism. The First Middle School is the largest in scale, with annual funding of over 130,000 yuan. Chen suddenly appointed Zeng Zhonglu, who was not familiar with the education community in Jiangxi, as the principal, and transferred the original principal Chen Yingchun to the Fourth Middle School. Zeng had been appointed as the director of the Mass Education Center last year, but resigned because he heard that the center had little funding. As a result, the faculty and staff of the First Middle School and the students who stayed on campus during the summer vacation petitioned the provincial government to retain Principal Chen. That day, Chen happened to be participating in the elementary school graduation exam award ceremony, and was surrounded and almost beaten. The Industrial College and other schools also had petitions. This was related to the replacement of principals. The abolition of the Second Girls' Middle School in Ganzhou and the integration of classes into the Third Middle School further angered the female community. On the 7th, they went to the Education Department and surrounded Chen, giving him unbearable treatment. Chen's abolition and merger of various schools and replacement of principals were not without reason, but the faculty and staff believed that education was a planned undertaking. Not only did it affect their livelihoods, but it also led to the degeneration of education. Therefore, the opposition was firm, which was beyond Chen's expectations. Because Chen planned to set up two independent normal schools, one in Nanchang and one in Ganzhou.

Training Course Regulations: (1) Name: This association is organized by the Shanghai County Social Education Research Association and is named the Shanghai County Summer Social Education Training Course. (2) Purpose: This association aims to utilize the summer vacation to facilitate the further education of social education service personnel and to enhance the academic theories and techniques of social education. (3) Organization: This association will have one honorary chairman and will be divided into three sections: education, general affairs, and compilation and review. Each section will have one director. When necessary, assistants may be hired. (4) Trainees: All social education service personnel in the county or others who are interested in studying social education, regardless of gender, may join the association and attend the lectures. (However, due to financial constraints, the limit is 30 people.) (5) Benefits: (A) Social education service personnel in the county should pay half the cost of meals, half a yuan and a half, and three yuan for full meals.

B) Those who are not serving in social education organizations but are interested in attending the lectures will be exempt from all board and lodging expenses. (C) Those from other counties who are interested in attending the lectures will receive the same treatment as social education service personnel in this county. (D) All baggage of the councilors must be self-provided. (6) Instructors: Instructors will be mainly social education experts from within the country, and will serve in an obligation way except the travel expenses. (7) Subjects: The subjects are divided into modern educational trends, mass literature and art, general introduction to mass political education (including a general introduction to local autonomy and cooperation), general introduction to rural sociology, rural economics, Party ideology, social issues, drama, and problem discussions, etc. (8) Duration: The training period of this association is tentatively set for two weeks, two hours each morning and afternoon (excluding discussion sessions). (9) Funding: Two-thirds will be allocated from the special social education funds of the Shanghai County Education Bureau, and the rest will be borne by various social education organizations. (10) Location: The principle is to be convenient for transportation and spacious. (11) These regulations will be implemented upon approval by the Education Bureau after passing through the Preparatory Committee of this Association. Gu Shusen is responsible for the instructor list (Modern Educational Trends) (Drama Practice I, Shen Yanbing (Mass Literature and Art) (Drama), Huan Yangyu Qian (Drama Practice), Lu Zhe (Party Ideology) Li Feng (Rural Sociology) (Mass Political Education)) Zhu Tongjiu (Rural Economics) Wang Fuquan (Modern Social Issues) (Drama).

Sports

The Past and Present of the World Games (7) 98

(7) The Relationship between the International Olympic Committee and the Far Eastern Athletic Association

The International Olympic Committee and the Far Eastern Athletic Association have the same goals, and the methods they use to achieve these goals are also the same, and both have been successful for many years. There should be a close relationship between them. The scope of the Olympic Committee is the entire world, but the opportunities for the development of sports in various countries around the world are quite unequal. It is not easy to achieve the realization of universal sports. Therefore, the Olympic Committee's ideas must have a development mechanism, must maintain the highest standards of amateur sports, and must promote universal sports as its purpose. As for the training of sports stars, it is accidental and not due to promotion.

The Far Eastern Athletic Association is a relatively young organization. It is no less than a child of the Olympic Committee. It has learned a lot from the Olympic Committee. For example, the order of the Far Eastern Games is as far as possible in accordance with the Olympic Games, except for those limited by the circumstances of each country. The current conference schedule has been changed to be held once every four years, and it is held in between the Olympic Games to avoid conflicts.

The original name of the Far Eastern Athletic Association was the Har Eastern Olympic Association. The western name of the Olympic Committee is Olympic Committee. Later, at the request of the Olympic Committee, the word Olympic was not used, and it was changed to the Far Eastern Athletic Association.

The current relationship between the two associations is not out of compulsion. The Olympic Committee does not restrict the Far Eastern Athletic Association, nor does it infringe on its privileges. The Far Eastern Athletic Association can therefore increase its reputation and influence through this relationship, and at the same time make the Olympic Committee have wider contact with the world's competitive situation. The Olympic Committee sends a commissioner to each Far Eastern Games as a special envoy, and appoints a famous athlete in each related country as a special representative of the Olympic Games to guide the events of the Far Eastern Games and promote its development.

At the beginning of the establishment of the Far Eastern Athletic Association, it was quite popular with the Olympic Committee.

Encouraged by the members of the Webber Committee, Professor Wm. Sloano, AV. Ormous, and F. J. Wendell, a golden wreath was presented to the Far Eastern Games as one of the trophy prizes. However, the Olympic Committee did not officially recognize the Far Eastern Games until 1920. The reason for the delay was the European War, so it was not that it did not approve or pay attention to this new international organization. That year, when the Olympic Committee held a regular meeting in Antwerp, E. S. Brown represented the Far Eastern Athletic Association and presented its objectives and achievements in detail. All the members fully agreed and decided to send Kano Jigoro as the official representative of the Olympic Committee to participate in the Far Eastern Games held in Shanghai in 1921. At that time, Kano was the only Far Eastern member of the Olympic Committee. At the opening of the 5th Far Eastern Games, he delivered a congratulatory speech on behalf of the Olympic Committee, explained the situation at the Antwerp Conference to the Far Eastern Games, and reported the results of the Shanghai Conference to the President of the Olympic Committee, Gubadin.

In the autumn of 1922, Count Peirandra de Coubertin, Vice President of the Olympic Committee (the current President), served as a special envoy and traveled from Europe to the United States to participate in the First Latin American Games held in the capital of Brazil in September. He also planned to go to Osaka, Japan to participate in the 6th Far Eastern Games in May 1923. His trip to South America was quite worthwhile. After the meeting, he traveled to various countries in South America to inspect the situation of physical education. He originally planned to travel around the Far East and finally to Osaka, Japan. Japan was also actively preparing to welcome him. However, when Pei was about to depart from South America, he suddenly received a telegram summoning him back to Europe due to important matters, so he did not make the trip. This was a great disappointment to the Far Eastern Games. Later, the President of the Olympic Games, Gubadin, expressed the hope that Dr. Wang Zhengting, the new member of the Olympic Committee, would represent the Olympic Committee at the 6th Far Eastern Games. However, Wang was unable to attend due to the critical nature of the Sino-Russian incident. Kano Jigoro was still representing the Olympic Committee in reading a congratulatory telegram at the opening ceremony.

After Japan's Sato, who reached the final four, won the doubles, the two singles matches were as completely defeated as Austin's. Stepheni's victory over Sangyuan was expected, while Palmeri suddenly surprisingly defeated Sato. Sato ran around in the last three sets, not knowing what to do. After the match, Sato was out of breath and exhausted and lost. The results of the two singles matches are listed below:

Free Talk

The Despotic Monkey 108

Most of the despotic countries in the world should be disappearing now. The revolution in Siam has been successful, and one more despotic country in the world has weakened.

A friend suddenly remembered a story about a despotic monkey after hearing me talk about despotism. According to him, he read it from the "Miscellaneous Records of Lingnan." I don't have this book on my desk, but I'll write down what my friend said:

In a certain mountain in Lingnan, there is a kind of despotic monkey, named Velvet, which is twice the size of an ordinary monkey and has golden fur. It is known as the demon king among monkeys. It usually feeds on apes and monkeys. When the Velvet wants to eat a monkey, it lets out a long roar, and the monkeys gather together after hearing the sound and kneel in front of the Velvet. The Velvet then examines each monkey for its fatness. The fatter ones pick up a small stone and put it on the monkey's head, and the monkey dares not move. The Velvet then lets out another long roar, and the rest of the monkeys all leave, but the monkey wearing the stone respectfully follows the Velvet to the river, washes itself in the water, and then plucks its own fur to make it clean. After plucking, it lies naked on the ground, allowing the Velvet to feast on it. The despotic magic power of the Velvet is so great!

After listening to this story, I sighed for a long time.

It's not a fable. Aren't there despotic demon kings like Velvet in the world now? The pitiful remnants of Jizi have become monkeys with stones on their heads, providing a feast for the demon king. The demon king, not satisfied with eating Koreans, wants to eat my compatriots outside the Guan. All the people who are willing to be devoured by the demon king are actually not people, but have become weaklings providing food for the strong.

Why did General Ma, who rises again and again, resist to the end? He was afraid of becoming a monkey with a stone on his head!

Ma Zhanshan and Feng Zhanhai Outside Shanhaiguan 109

— Wu Cai Zhi

Since the September 18th Incident in Northeast China, half of our country has been occupied by foreign countries for a long time. The day to return my invaded land is nowhere in sight. Fortunately, Black Chairman Ma Zhanshan and Jiyi Army Feng Zhanhai were the first to raise the banner of righteousness and resist the strong enemy with all their might. He healed the wounded and supported the weak, and raised his arms and called out to strive for the last five minutes and make a desperate gamble. Success or failure is difficult to predict, but the prestige is enough to shock people. Don't say that there is no one in Qin. Make them fear Shu like tigers. What is strange is that Ma is named Zhanshan and Feng is named Zhanhai. One is to show the remaining courage of Fu Bo and mark the bronze pillar for long-term existence, and the other is to rely on the legacy of the big tree to consolidate the golden cup forever. Heaven and man respond, and the names and treasures are consistent. He will wield a hundred thousand horizontal grinders and hold three thousand Mauser rifles. He will travel as fast as a meteor, and encompass everything. He will restore all the land, people, and politics outside the three Guan, across the Bai Mountains in eastern China and the Liaohai Sea in northern China, to my nation, and return my sovereignty, and occupy them all. In the past, someone had a couplet saying: "Those who have the will will succeed. Break the cauldrons and sink the boats. The one hundred and twenty Qin passes will eventually belong to Chu. Hard work will not be in vain. Lying on firewood and tasting gall. The six thousand Yue armor is enough to swallow Wu." Know what to strive for. Don't be discouraged.

Physiological Oddity 110

— Sent by Peng Licheng from Nanchang

Recently in Nanchang, a strange physiological anomaly occurred, causing a sensation in society. Various newspapers raced to report it. The matter is so bizarre that I am recording it for this column for research purposes.

In Fengcheng County, more than a hundred miles from Nanchang, a young newly married couple, on their wedding night, naturally indulged in marital bliss, fulfilling the duty of marriage. Unexpectedly, upon their initial exploration of paradise, they lost the freedom to separate, as if experiencing a kind of attraction like that in physics. Although both tried to separate, they could not succeed. By daybreak, after being discovered by family members, they were sent to a local hospital for treatment. Due to the lack of skilled doctors in the area, no one dared to make a diagnosis without caution. They were then taken to the Saint Church Hospital in Nanchang City, known for its reputation, for treatment. However, the hospital found this kind of physiological anomaly quite unprecedented and felt very perplexed about the treatment. Besides surgical separation, there was no other method. Therefore, with the consent of both sets of parents, surgery was performed. However, before the surgery, the hospital declared that only one of the two could be guaranteed safe; otherwise, it was beyond medical capability. As a result of the operation, the male was fortunate enough to be safe, but the female, due to being beyond saving, died tragically in a pool of blood. It is said that from the wedding day to the day of surgery, nearly a week had passed. During this period, their bodies were closely connected, and even urination and defecation could not be separated at all, flowing down their legs, which was indeed a bitter situation. Now, after hearing the news, medical professionals in Nanchang have flocked to the hospital requesting public observation. However, the hospital doctors stated that such a physiological anomaly is rarely heard of, and there is a lack of research on treatment methods. As for performing surgery, it was out of necessity, so they have not agreed to public observation. One wonders if there are many good Chinese and Western doctors in Shanghai who can explain the reason for this.

The Taste of Plums 111

— Qing Qu

I am fond of plums. Others who see me eat them find their teeth ache and their mouths water, and they avoid me as if I were a plague. But when I eat them, I find them quite delicious. Indeed, the Compendium of Materia Medica lists their medicinal value, and the Treatise on Various Flowers and Fruits even has a discussion of cooking plums. This shows that plums, as a food item, simply haven’t been studied. If someone with a scientific mind were to utilize them, they could certainly become a good food product, greatly benefitting human life.

This year's plum harvest is more abundant than last year’s. People commonly refer to this as a ripe year. In truth, there was little snowfall last winter. Even the plum trees of Luofu and Yuling Mountains, which prefer warmth, have ancient trunks in famous gardens and old temples that are twisted and sparse, but covered with fruit. It is not just our county that has this phenomenon. Last year, a catty could be sold for a dime, and the demand still exceeded the supply. Now, only four or five copper coins can be obtained per catty, and yet no one inquires about them. The disparity is quite great. Moreover, due to the war, sugar prices are too high, and the weather is mostly overcast and rainy, so there are even fewer buyers. In the past, people thought plums were easy to cultivate, and planting them was simple. Those who first promoted them as excellent garden plants would say, "Plums three, peaches four," meaning plum seedlings would produce profit after three years. Now the opposite is true. It is not known that the practical uses of plums are extremely broad. Since their value is low, it is a great pity to let them go to waste.

During the time of avoiding the war, I went to Zhuxi and saw shops selling pickled plum skins. At first, I found it strange. Later, I inquired with a gentleman there and learned that it was a local specialty. I bought some and ate it; the taste was very good, but it was too sweet, and the original flavor was lost. The so-called “clear water” (pickled) plum was not its true flavor. Each year, sales of these pickled plums, while not a major commodity, generate significant profits. It made me think that the most common food product using plums is dried tangerine peel plum. But now, those who make this substitute other ingredients because of the profits involved, the name is correct, but the substance is not. If one has a sense of taste, one can distinguish the real from the fake with just one taste. In fact, the manufacturing method is extremely easy. Try using 100 catties of plums, 10% edible salt, place them in pottery, making sure they are evenly distributed. After about three days, add fresh water to reduce the salty taste. Then drain the water and soak the plum embryos in a 50% sugar solution for about a day. The acidic taste will gradually disappear and neutralize with the sugar, making it delicious to eat. The uses of this are far more extensive than plum sauce, plum paste, plum candy, plum cakes, and dried plums, plum jam, as well as cold noodles, cherries, and pudding. The additional ingredients only require licorice, cloves, mint, ginger powder, and star anise. Adding lemon or a small amount of fragrant powder to blend it further enhances the taste. Our county’s plum production is later than elsewhere. If we could manufacture it during the plum ripening season, it would also be a good household item for clearing heat and preventing foulness.

A Record of the War Zone Relics Painting Exhibition 112

— Kang

There are many people who have taken photographs of the relics of the Shanghai War Zone. Few have captured them in paintings. Before the armistice, Japan had already sent famous painters Wada Sanzo, Okada Saburo, etc. to Shanghai by the army and navy authorities to paint many works in situ. These were then taken to Tokyo for exhibition. After the armistice agreement, our country only then had the famous painter Wang Jiyuan personally request Mayor Wu to introduce him to Yin Yilin, Chairman of the troop withdrawal and takeover committee, to issue a certificate. He began to paint the ruins in Jiangwan, Zhabei, Wusong, and Baoshan, braving wind and rain and intense sun. After repeated difficulties, Wang created dozens of watercolor paintings, which are truly valuable. Wang has started an exhibition on the second floor of the Jiyuan Art Studio at 90 Luban Road, McSaillard Road, from the 9th for six days. The exhibition is open to the public from 1 pm to 7 pm daily. On the opening day, Wang Jingqi impromptu composed a seven-character quatrain, inscribed in the Jiyuan commemorative album, containing the line: “Recalling the setting sun on the ruined walls, each stroke of the brush accompanied by a tear of blood.”

Worth Introducing National Goods Factories (3) 113

— He Gongxing

(4) Type Foundries

The type used in printing factories is mostly purchased from type foundries. There are dozens of these type foundries in Shanghai. In addition to the Commercial Press, China Bookstore, World Bookstore, etc., the Huafeng Type Foundry on Renji Bridge is the largest. Newspaper offices such as Shen Xin, etc., in addition to casting type for their own use, can also sell it to others.

The most important part of type is the matrix. The quality of the type is often determined by the depth and uniformity of the engraving on the copper matrix, as well as the neatness and elegance of the font. Most of these matrices used to come from Japan. In recent years, Chinese people have also been able to manufacture them. There are more than a dozen such factories in the whole of Shanghai, the most famous being Wang Zhen's in Zhabei. However, it is still a step behind Japanese goods. Therefore, when large printing houses and newspapers need matrices, they still mostly purchase them from Japan. It is hoped that craftsmen in this industry will pay attention to this.

Type is divided into two types: high and low. The high type is called the "continental style" and uses the German typeface as the standard. The low type is called the "island style" and uses the English and American typeface as the standard. Therefore, buyers must specify which type they want; otherwise, the type they buy will be different in height from the existing type and cannot be typeset. However, Chinese type mostly uses the island style. Western type varies from company to company, so buyers must pay attention.

When manufacturing type, first install the matrix in the type casting machine, then adjust its height and match it with the type case. Old-fashioned type casting machines are hand-cranked, with each crank producing only one character. The characters produced all have tails, which must be removed. Then a small planer is used to plane it smooth, and a grinder is used to polish it before it can be used. New type casting machines are driven by motors. The characters produced can be used immediately without planing or grinding. A hand-cranked machine costs only a hundred yuan or so. An automatic one costs ten thousand yuan. The best automatic type casting machines are the Kesmen factory products managed by the German firm Taylor in Shanghai. American products are second best. German machines can produce typefaces from number one to number seven, casting three to four thousand characters per hour. American goods cannot cast as many as seven types. Old-fashioned hand-cranked machines can only cast a hundred or so characters per hour, a difference of almost twenty times. It was previously heard that the Jianye Machinery Factory in Zhabei, our country, had already begun to imitate German goods, but before it was completed, it was burned to the ground by war. It is regrettable.

Type is sold by the pound, with each pound costing thirty to forty cents. Smaller typefaces are more expensive. The lead used for type casting is all foreign goods. If it were made entirely of lead, the type would not be strong and durable. A little copper, tin, and antimony must be added. Approximately 3% copper and tin and 7% antimony.

Records of Striking the Bell in an Ancient Temple (4) (8) 114

— Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhai Fu (The Man Who Does Not Weed His Courtyard)

Fifty-two

I feel that my bell-ringing duty has become even more meaningful during these times. Life in the ancient temple seems inextricably linked to the sound of the bell that I strike. Take the military and martial arts training, for example; it cannot do without the bell. We don't have trumpets or bugles. This large bell has taken their place, performing the task of issuing commands. Because everyone is working hard, I am also ringing the bell with energy. However, the farmers say that because I am ringing the bell with energy, they are working hard. Most likely, both sides are right: working hard makes one ring the bell with energy, and ringing the bell with more energy makes one work even harder.

Tonight, Battalion Commander Huang, Mr. Zhu, Company Commander Jiang, and Master Zhang secretly decided to issue an emergency assembly order at midnight for a night battle drill. No one else in the entire village knows this secret. Even I don't know there will be such a charade tonight. The emergency assembly order is three loud, rapid strikes of the bell. Whenever this kind of bell sound is heard, everyone must immediately jump out of bed, grab the weapons they are responsible for guarding, and run to their designated locations to await orders. Those who are absent or late without reason, or who forget to bring the weapons they are responsible for guarding, or who run to the wrong locations will be severely punished. At eleven fifty, they dragged me out of bed, wanting me to strike this emergency assembly bell, which I had never struck before. Although this was unexpected, I had long anticipated it. How happy I was! As soon as the bell rang, wives pushed husbands, sisters-in-law shouted for uncles, older sisters called for younger brothers, and mothers called for sons, all saying that bandits had arrived, get up quickly! Everyone, according to the distance from their homes, in three, five, seven, or ten minutes, arrived at their predetermined positions, awaiting orders. Only then did they realize that tonight was a drill and not a real bandit raid. But the drill was still carried out as seriously.

Mr. Zhu had already planned this out. He had been inquiring which families had elderly people and which had sick people. At first, I didn't know what he was up to. Before waking me up, he specially sent several people to inform the elderly and the sick in advance so that they would not be frightened.

Battalion Commander Huang had previously told everyone that bandits sometimes set fires on the west side while looting on the east side. Suddenly, we saw a fire break out on the opposite side, half the sky was red. Although they sent some people to put out the fire, the main force remained calm and composed.

Gold Price Plunges Over Eight Taels 116

The falling trend is very strong. Yesterday, the benchmark gold price continued its downward trend, almost breaking the 750 tael mark. However, the market situation was complicated, and the mentality of the industry turned downward. Throughout the day, there was a fluctuation of 14 taels. Finally, the total drop was eight taels and change. Initially, it was peaceful, and the silver price rose slightly, so it did not have an impact. However, seeing that there were many buyers, it should have trended upward. However, the cashiers of various firms diverged, and the exchange rate was flat externally but weak internally, so the price immediately dropped. There were occasional bounces of two or three taels. As the exchange rate hardened in the afternoon, and the selling pressure increased, the market price continued to decline, finally falling to 750 taels. In the end, it fluctuated between 53 taels. The details of the market situation before and after are recorded below.

The morning market was mild. The opening price for August fell by only four qian to 761 taels. Large bars rose by only 3/16 to 1/8, and American silver rose by only 1/8. There were few Yin Yuan-denominated goods and sales were small. The market was stable. Twenty or thirty boats arrived from the west road, with about 2,000 stones of river-bottom rice.

The Fuzhou Group Trialed a Batch Yesterday

The Tianjin Group purchased 20,000 bags of paoche flour, priced at 1 liang 9 qian.

New York Raw Silk Sales Greatly Reduced 131

Less than 40,000 bales last month: Japanese silk accounted for 76%

New York has many silk weaving factories, and the annual consumption of raw silk requires more than 50,000 bales. Since the global economic recession, the sales of silk have plummeted, and the consumption of raw silk has greatly reduced. The consumption of silk in the last month (June) totaled only about 38,000 bales, a reduction of about 30%. Japanese silk accounted for 76%, and the remainder was from China, Austria, Italy, France, and other countries.

Local News

Huang Bingheng Hosts Banquet for All Sectors to Discuss Aviation to Save the Nation 134

Huang Bingheng, Director of the Aviation Administration, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday. At 7 pm yesterday, he hosted a banquet at the Bankers' Association, inviting leaders from all sectors to discuss matters related to the Aviation to Save the Nation Association and to plan for expanding aviation projects. Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Li Fusun, and dozens of others attended. During the banquet, Director Huang delivered a speech, saying that during the Anti-Japanese War, domestic civil groups and overseas Chinese had requested the National Government to quickly establish an Aviation to Save the Nation Association to lead the people and assist the government. The National Government then ordered the aviation authorities to adopt public opinion and coordinate methods. Since the Aviation Administration was instructed to handle this case, it sent its specialist committee member, Lin Wojang, to Shanghai a few weeks ago to visit everyone, explain the reasons for organizing the Aviation to Save the Nation Association, and solicit opinions. He was grateful for everyone's support. He was very happy and came to meet everyone in person for further consultation. He hoped that the Aviation to Save the Nation Association could be established soon through the efforts of both sides, so that the public and the government could have a fully cooperative center for aviation and air defense. The organization law of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association, the future direction, and the steps to be taken are entirely hoped to be determined by social leaders. If there is a need for aviation experts to participate in discussions, the Aviation Administration will order them to offer advice for adoption. As for the draft charter of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association prepared by the Aviation Administration, it only represents the government's perspective and the concept of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association. It is still desired to wait for everyone to discuss and determine it at a meeting. Whether the board of directors is organized automatically first and then the charter is submitted to the National Government for record, or the charter is first submitted to the National Government by the competent authority for promulgation and then directors are appointed, is acceptable. The draft charter can be regarded as a reference material. The origin of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association is roughly like this. As for its significance and the necessity of this organization, I would like to briefly explain one or two points. The air force is definitely in the most important position in today's strategy because (1) war has evolved from a plane to a three-dimensional space. In the past, offense and defense were limited to land and sea, but now the solution of victory or defeat depends on the sky. Therefore, fortresses that were regarded as natural barriers in the past are almost equivalent to illusions. (2) In the past, the targets of attack were the enemy's military buildings and front-line combatants, but now the air force constantly crosses the battle line to attack civilians in the rear and material construction outside the battlefield. Therefore, innocent people and prosperous areas cannot avoid being destroyed together. During this anti-Japanese war, our side suffered severe damage from the enemy's air force. Therefore, the organization of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association can be regarded as a new understanding of the government and the people after this violent suppression to find a way out. In other words, we have recently understood the value of the air force in strategy and fully understand that unless we combine the strength of the government and the people to seek to develop our country's aviation industry, then with a few dozen aircraft that are not fully equipped, resisting the enemy's air force, which is a dozen to dozens of times more powerful, destruction can be expected immediately, let alone resistance. Today, our country's authorities may not know that expanding the air force is an urgent task. In the past two months, the government has slightly increased the aviation budget. The Aviation Administration is also making great efforts to expand the aviation school to train air force personnel, rectify the aviation factory, and enrich the various aviation teams. However, due to the lack of financial resources and talent, it is ultimately difficult to promote. Looking at the urgent situation in Guanwai and the increasingly fierce banditry in the Central Plains, the development is limited by strength, and the encroachment of foreign aggression is unpredictable, and I am truly concerned. Fortunately, many civil groups at home and abroad understand the overall situation and work together to enable our country to form a powerful air force in the near future. I am willing to take the responsibility of carrying out the task together with leaders from all parties with full enthusiasm. However, since the majority of the directors of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association are representatives of people from all parties, the direction of the project should be controlled by the board of directors. Aviation is a powerful tool for national defense, so there must be a strict review of policies and strategies and a complete plan. This is the government's inescapable responsibility. In the future, how much the public wants the air force to develop, how to raise funds to facilitate the project, and how the government plans and budgets for national defense can all be used as a center for exchanging ideas, gathering ideas, and taking action. The establishment of the Aviation to Save the Nation Association and the cooperation between the government and the people will be realized. Subsequently, Huang discussed the progress of the association with various dignitaries and did not disperse until 9 o'clock.

Municipal Government Prepares for Autonomy 135

Minutes of the Preparatory Committee's Two Resolutions

The Shanghai Municipal Autonomy Preparatory Committee was established on the 1st of this month and held its first meeting at the Municipal Government. The following seven committee members were present: Yu Hongjun, Wu Xingya, Yang Nianzu, Xu Peihuang, Luo Jingyou, Wang Zhijing, and Shen Tong. Yu Hongjun chaired the meeting. The meeting began with a report by the chairman on the progress of the municipal autonomy preparations. This was followed by a report from Committee Member Wu on the steps for preparing autonomy, and a report from Committee Member Xu on the progress of district demarcation work. After the reports, the following resolutions were discussed and decided: (1) Pass the committee's procedural rules; (2) For the selection of the heads of each group, the Secretariat will send personnel for the General Affairs Group, the Public Security Bureau will select personnel for the Investigation Group, and the Social Affairs Bureau will select personnel for the Election Group. The list of names will be sent to the chairman for appointment and reporting on the following day; (3) Yu and Shen will be delegated to compile the committee's budget; (4) The Public Security Bureau will be requested to order each district office to submit a report on changes in the wartime household registration to the committee within one week, after which it will be decided whether to re-demarcate the districts; (5) The meeting date for the committee will be set for every Friday at 10:00 AM. Because there was no suitable location for the committee office, it was temporarily located in the Municipal Government Building. Several rooms have now been located in the Diplomatic Building and the office moved there yesterday to officially begin work. The second meeting was held at 3:00 PM yesterday. All committee members were present except for Luo Jingyou, who requested leave due to business, and Wu Xingya, who was represented by Huang Baoshi. Yu Hongjun chaired the meeting. The subject of discussion was the progress of the Investigation Group's work, and a detailed discussion was held based on the draft plan prepared by the group. It was also resolved that when conducting household registration surveys, the investigation of voter qualifications should also be emphasized. For the investigation of those who have committed crimes and been deprived of their civil rights, a letter has been sent to the Shanghai courts requesting records to be sent to the committee for review. A decision was also made to conduct a household registration survey in the Special District within a set period, but the method has not yet been determined. The Investigation Group's work plan is recorded below:

(1) Set up district boundary markers to demarcate the city's autonomous districts. The previous district demarcation committee, based on the number of registered households in July of the 19th year, and based on the number of households re-examined as the standard, with the exception of the four districts of Huinan, Zhabei, Yangjing, and Yinxiang, where ten households form a neighborhood and ten thousand households form a district due to special circumstances, all other districts are demarcated in accordance with the Municipal Organization Law, with five households as a neighborhood and five thousand households as a district, dividing the city into forty districts, and detailed maps of the district boundaries have been drawn. For the convenience of the work, boundary markers (such as the boundary of a certain district) will be made for these forty districts (including the war zones) and nailed at the boundaries of each district to facilitate investigation.

(2) Investigate household registration. Although the city's household registration has been investigated and sampled by the Municipal Public Security Bureau, due to the city's rapid changes, which are unparalleled in the country, there are bound to be changes and errors. These should be investigated immediately to avoid disputes during elections. The methods are as follows: (1) After the district boundary markers are nailed, personnel will be sent to each area to investigate each household to avoid omissions. (2) After completing the investigation of one street or one village, continue to process the household registration register and send personnel to re-examine it, and it must be checked against the Public Security Bureau's master register of household registration changes. If there is any doubt, it should be investigated immediately. (3) After the investigation is completed, statistics should be compiled separately in order to start dividing neighborhoods.

(3) Investigate boundary changes. In the demarcation of the city into forty districts, if there are special circumstances in the number of households in each district, each district should not exceed 10,300 households at most, and at least around 90 households, with the remainder being based on 5,000 households, not exceeding 6,000 households. However, the number of households in non-war zones such as Huinan and Yangjing has been increasing, while the number of households in war zones such as Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, Yinhang, and Zhenru may decrease. However, the boundary of other districts should not be affected by the change in the number of households in a small number of districts. The proposed methods are as follows: 1. In areas where the number of households has increased, the previous number of households can still be used as the standard, and the increased number of households will be incorporated into adjacent areas where the number of households has decreased. 2. Areas where the number of households has decreased can be merged depending on the number of households decreased.

(4) Survey and examine district boundary maps. After the household registration investigation is completed and the district boundaries are demarcated, the area should be measured immediately and detailed maps should be drawn for examination.

(5) Handle household registration changes. After the household registration investigation is completed in a district, citizens often change their place of residence. Personnel should be sent to manage this to ensure accuracy. There are two methods to choose from: 1. Send personnel from each sub-office to manage it specifically. 2. Or it can still be managed by the original household registration officers in each district of the Public Security Bureau. When there are changes, the sub-office should be notified daily for correction and reporting to avoid confusion over time.

Japanese Troops in District D Repeatedly Delay Withdrawal 136

Yu Hongjun Asks Ke Nanninghan to Expedite the Process

The Japanese troops in District D and the Gongda and Toyota textile factories have not yet withdrawn. The two Chinese members of the Joint Committee, Yu Hongjun and Wen Yingxing, have repeatedly negotiated with the Japanese side, but have not received a satisfactory reply. Committee Member Yu Hongjun formally sent a letter to Ke Nanninghan, chairman of the Joint Committee, requesting that the Japanese side withdraw as soon as possible. Subsequently, Ke invited the Chinese member Yu Hongjun and the Japanese member Okazaki to meet at the US consulate on the morning of the 6th to discuss the matter. As a result, Okazaki agreed to give a definite reply to the Chinese side within three days regarding the date of withdrawal of the Japanese troops from District D. As for the Japanese troops in the Gongda and Toyota textile factories, they will be withdrawn successively after the withdrawal from District D is completed. However, the agreed deadline of three days passed the day before yesterday, but there was no reply from the Japanese side. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Committee Member Yu Hongjun yesterday to inquire about this matter. According to Yu, the Japanese member Okazaki promised to reply within three days when he met with him at the US consulate on the 6th regarding the definite date of withdrawal of the Japanese troops from District D, but as of today (the 11th), two days have passed the agreed deadline of three days, and he has not yet received a reply from the Japanese side. The Japanese side's repeated delays and intentional breach of the agreement clearly violate the spirit of the agreement. Therefore, he notified Ke Nanninghan, chairman of the Joint Committee, by telephone at 11:00 AM today (i.e., yesterday), requesting that he urge the Japanese side to withdraw as soon as possible and notify the Chinese side of the definite date of withdrawal.

The Money Trade Association Hosted Newspaper Reporters Last Night 138

Regarding the Abolition of Taels and the Change to Yuan,

Repeated emphasis on the need for seriousness

The Shanghai Money Trade Association hosted newspaper reporters at 7:00 PM yesterday at the association's office on Ningbo Road to discuss the issue of abolishing taels and changing to yuan. More than 40 reporters from various newspapers and news agencies attended. Qin Runqing, chairman of the association, presided over the meeting, and Yu Zuoting, Fu Songnian, and Hu Xisheng, all standing committee members, successively gave reports. The meeting adjourned at 4:00 PM. The details are recorded below:

Qin Runqing reported. The chairman of the association, Qin Runqing, reported first, saying, "Today, our association invited reporters from various newspapers to gather together. We are very honored that you have taken the time to come despite the sweltering heat. This time, the Ministry of Finance has made a decision to abolish taels and change to yuan. Our association agrees with the principle. However, after the change to yuan, the most important issue is to unify the currency system, so as not to cause hundreds of problems because of one benefit. Therefore, we telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to adopt our opinions a few days ago. However, there are many people outside who do not understand, thinking that the money trade is opposed to abolishing taels and changing to yuan. In fact, the money trade has repeatedly explained before that what we require is to rectify the currency system. The situation of the money trade is slightly different from other financial circles. It has a history of hundreds of years and has always focused on providing credit loans as its main business. If shops need to buy goods, etc., villagers must buy and sell in cash, so credit loans are necessary for trade. As for the advantages and disadvantages of the future currency system, Minister Song has said that after the establishment of the Central Mint in the future, a fair valuation must be researched for the fineness of the new currency. If this can be done, hard currency can be unified. However, the most dangerous thing is still paper money. If the fund reserves are insufficient, once a panic occurs due to political relations, it will inevitably cause unimaginable harm to society. Therefore, several meetings have been held for the overall consideration of society, and we must first seek to unify the currency system. The gentlemen of the press present here are all opinion leaders in society, and we hope that they will uphold justice."

Yu Zuoting reported. Yu Zuoting reported, saying, "Unifying the currency system was initiated in the late Qing Dynasty, and it has not been implemented for decades. It is heartbreaking to say. Although it is due to frequent internal turmoil, most of it is due to the lack of unified issuance. Private banks all have the right to issue currency, and the government does not ask whether the issuance reserves of each bank comply with the law. During the January 28th Incident in Shanghai, money shops in the interior operated as usual, but the issuance could not be redeemed. We have doubts. The true meaning of abolishing taels and changing to yuan is not to borrow its name to promote its reality. We must know that the issuance of currency in China, such as the suspension of redemption by the Sino-French Bank in Tianjin, Hankou, harmed the commercial market. In recent years, the Dongpiao, Jiangqian, and Jitie in the three northeastern provinces have plummeted in market value, and the bank notes of Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, and Zhili provinces are almost worthless. Prices have soared, and farmers and merchants have gone bankrupt. Shanghai's successive incidents have been able to weather the storm because of the silver cash market. If taels are abolished and yuan are changed, and the hard currency is insufficient, soft currency will inevitably replace it. Once the market changes, I am afraid that it will repeat the mistakes of Tianjin and Hankou, or even follow in the footsteps of Russia and Germany. Moreover, since the January 28th Incident, the Shanghai market has been chaotic, and the financial situation has not recovered. The state of depression has affected the whole country, forming a social and national poverty. If we suddenly change course, it will cause public unrest and panic in the market. If we implement the abolition of taels and the change to yuan, we should ask the government to first unify the currency power and the right to issue currency, and then follow the example of the United States and the United Kingdom to fully prepare for the policy of gradually unifying the currency system, so as not to shake the market."

The Franco-Chinese Water and Electricity Labor Strike Yesterday 139

French Consul Visits Mayor Wu

Arrested Workers Immediately Released

After the strike by the employees of the Mechanical Department of the Franco-Chinese Water and Electricity Company, consultations between the municipal government and the French consul yielded no results. The attitudes of both labor and management are extremely rigid, and the strike is bound to be prolonged. The union's employee department held an emergency meeting yesterday and issued a declaration. The various situations are recorded below:

Reduction in the number of vehicles due to damage. Yesterday was the fifth day of the strike. Due to the impact of the strike by the Mechanical Department, tramcars and buses of the Franco-Chinese Water and Electricity Company were damaged and no one was repairing them. Many damaged tramcars and buses were parked in the factory on Luban Road. For example, Route 10 from Lujiawan to the 16th Pier, which originally had eight vehicles, has now been reduced to four vehicles. Route 6, which originally had six vehicles, has now been reduced to two vehicles. As for Route 1 from the 16th Pier to the Zhaojiabang Road, Route 2 from the 16th Pier to Xujiahui, Route 3 from Xiaodongmen to Ximen, Route 4 from Tilanqiao to Zhaojiabang Road, Route 7 from the 16th Pier to Zhaojiabang Road, Route 18 from Xieqiao to Yuezhou Road, etc., the number of vehicles running has been reduced. The number of Route 21 buses has also been slightly reduced.

The course of consultations by the municipal government. After the Franco-Chinese Water and Electricity labor strike was reported to the municipal government by the Social Affairs Bureau, the municipal government immediately sent Secretary Geng Jiaji to meet with French Consul General Meyrier to discuss mediation methods. When Geng Jiaji met with Consul Meyrier, he briefly stated the municipal government's purpose, saying, "The Franco-Chinese Water and Electricity labor strike, the company is a Franco-Chinese company, and the location is in the French Concession. The municipal government originally had no need to interfere. However, the workers are all Chinese, and the number of people is large. In order to achieve a balanced solution and local security as soon as possible, we specifically seek your consul's opinion on whether your consul and the municipal government can jointly mediate to facilitate an early resumption of work and avoid expansion." The French consul replied that this was a disciplinary issue for the company. If dismissing a worker caused so much difficulty, there was really no way to resolve it, and the company's attitude was also very firm. Therefore, there was no substantial result. In addition, French Consul Meyrier visited Mayor Wu at 5:00 PM yesterday to have some contact.

Arrested workers immediately released. The Propaganda Section of the Second Water and Electricity Union Strike Committee yesterday ordered all its members to carry a large number of slogans and distribute them for posting in the Nanshi area, such as "(Down with the scab and traitor Lu Guanhong!)", "(Oppose the company's unjustified dismissal of workers!)", "(Down with imperialism!)", "(Support the Strike Committee!)", etc. As a result, the trams of the Franco-Chinese Routes 3, 5, and 6 and the walls were full of slogans. At 1:00 PM, worker Xue Wanshan was arrested by the police officers of the First Police Station of the Public Security Bureau near Xiaodongmen for posting slogans. After receiving the report, the union immediately sent Zhang Fubao to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to request his release. Xu Yefu, chief of the Third Section of the Bureau, sent Zhu Guilin to the Public Security Bureau together with Zhou Lianze of the Municipal Party Headquarters. Wang Zhijing, chief of the Second Section, notified the First Police Station to release him at 5:00 PM.

The union held a talk meeting yesterday. The Second Water and Electricity Union held a talk meeting at Dadali, Luban Road, at 1:00 PM yesterday. More than 800 members attended, and the surrounding area was maintained by the picket team. Shen Jing, of the Strike Committee, first reported on the negotiations between the municipal government's secretary Geng Jiaji and the French consul, and advised the members to strictly abide by order and wait patiently for the mediation of the party and government organs. As long as all members are united, they will surely achieve final victory.

Emergency meeting of employees. Due to the fact that the French Electricity Company's Chinese employees withdrew from the union as reported in various newspapers, the Employee Department of the Second Water and Electricity Union convened an emergency meeting of the Employee Department at the union in the morning. More than 60 people attended, and all said that this kind of fellowship association must be a small number of bad elements who listened lightly to blind words and were deliberately tempted by the capitalists to undermine the labor movement. In addition to absolutely denying the union's organization, they also issued a declaration.

The union solemnly declares. The Second Water and Electricity Union Mechanical Department members solemnly declare and refute the illegal organization of the fellowship association.

The original petition is recorded as follows: "Petition for the matter of the association. Repeated reasonable requests have been rejected with insults and curses, resulting in unbearable circumstances. They had no choice but to implement a strike starting on the 1st of this month and have submitted a request to the party and government organs for mediation. The capitalist is inherently cunning, resulting in no results. (Omitted) All members have come to petition and humbly request to be received so that they may state everything and request that personnel be dispatched to lead them and transfer to higher levels to petition, requesting prompt and impartial mediation to avoid further expansion of the dispute." For this reason, a document has been prepared, and two comrades, Fang Qinghe and others, have been sent as representatives to accompany all the employees of Feng Cunrentang to your ministry for petition, handing in the document in person, humbly requesting to be received for public convenience.

Emergency meeting of the association. The Traditional Chinese Medicine Trade Association has recently received secret reports from its members that the Pharmaceutical Vocational Union has dispatched cadres to various district branches and store groups to guide and prepare for a city-wide general strike, including the method and it is scheduled to be convened on the 17th of this month, the union will hold general assembly of all members. During the previous large-scale strikes in the pharmaceutical industry, the union would first set a date to convene a general meeting of members, and after the meeting, the employees would not return to the store to implement a general strike. Therefore, the union's convening of a general meeting of members on the 17th is no different from a general mobilization for a general strike. However, during this summer epidemic prevention period, if the union blatantly disregards social public health and insists on implementing a general strike, it will endanger society. The association is making appropriate prevention measures and held an emergency meeting of the executive committee at 2:00 PM this afternoon to discuss preventing the union from launching a general strike. At the same time, it appointed two responsible representatives of the association to attend the mediation meeting of the Social Affairs Bureau.

The party and government will question today. In order to prevent the expansion of the pharmaceutical labor unrest, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau will convene the Pharmaceutical Union and the National Medicine Trade Association for questioning at 1:00 PM this afternoon, together with the Municipal Party Headquarters, in order to conduct mediation. The notification is recorded below: "Notification for the matter of the pharmaceutical labor dispute. It is hereby decided to convene a questioning session at 1:00 PM on the afternoon of July 12. It is hereby ordered that the association send two responsible representatives to attend on time to listen to the questioning. This is hereby notified. July 10, 21st year of the Republic of China, Wu Xingya, Director."

The Shanghai Municipal Council's Special Board Meeting Approves the Principle of Returning Extraterritorial Roads 141

Passed with a vote of seven to six to accept

Progress was made in the continued consultations between the two parties last night

After the draft agreement on resolving the extraterritorial roads of the Shanghai International Settlement was submitted by Stirling Fessenden, Director-General of the Shanghai Municipal Council, for discussion at a special board meeting last Wednesday, the principle of accepting it was passed at that time. The remaining issues were only a few minor revisions to one of the items and wording. Last night, the representatives of both parties consulted once again, and some progress was made. The news obtained yesterday is recorded below:

The principle of returning was approved. According to reliable sources, at the special board meeting convened by the Shanghai Municipal Council last Wednesday to discuss the draft agreement on extraterritorial roads, all directors expressed considerable opinions. After a vote, it was formally approved with seven votes to six to accept the principle of returning the extraterritorial roads to China. There are fourteen directors on the Shanghai Municipal Council. The Director-General has no voting rights during peacetime, but if one of the directors gives up their vote due to an opinion or other reason, and the number of affirmative and negative votes cast by the remaining directors is the same, then the Director-General can participate in one vote. Therefore, at the special board meeting last Wednesday, excluding the vote of Director-General Bell, the remaining thirteen votes were passed with seven votes to six.

The content has been confirmed. The content of the three draft agreements previously published by the New Sound Society are: (1) All extraterritorial roads of the Shanghai International Settlement will be completely returned to the administration of the Chinese government. (2) After the extraterritorial roads are returned to the administration of the Chinese government, all police powers and other matters relating to the roads will also be returned to the administration of the Chinese government. However, in view of the large number of foreigners residing near the extraterritorial roads, both parties agree to establish a special police agency, with the Chinese government appointing a Chinese person as police chief and simultaneously appointing a foreigner approved by the Shanghai Municipal Council as deputy police chief. Underneath them, there will be a number of Chinese and foreign police officers, all of whom will be appointed by the Chinese government to serve in their respective positions. (3) The various taxes collected within the extraterritorial roads will be used to cover all expenses of the special police agency and the construction of roads. The administration of these taxes will be jointly responsible by the municipal government and the Shanghai Municipal Council. If there is a shortage of funds, the municipal government and the Shanghai Municipal Council will be jointly responsible for supplementing it equally. After many inquiries, the above three items have been completely confirmed and are generally accurate. However, the matter of the police chief and deputy police chief jointly handling disputes between Chinese and foreigners is confirmed to be inaccurate because it conflicts with the Shanghai International Settlement Special District Court Agreement. The points still need to be discussed. The Chinese side has received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and instructed Yu Hongjun to propose three revisions. It is now heard that there are not many problems. Only the Shanghai Municipal Council still requires some revisions to the wording and a certain item. It is said that this item is extremely important.

The two parties met last night. Director Fessenden of the Shanghai Municipal Council has been ill for several days, preventing a meeting. Mr. Fessenden had originally agreed with Yu Hongjun to go to the Municipal Government at 10:00 AM this morning, but he could not leave the house due to pain. The meeting was changed to 3:30 PM at Mr. Fessenden's private residence, but at 3:30 PM, Mr. Fessenden was still unable to receive guests. It was agreed that Mr. , Director of the Shanghai Municipal Council, would represent Mr. Fessenden and meet with Mr. Yu at 5:00 PM. It is heard that the result has made some progress.
