Sino-British Beam Communication Notice 144

Can be realized in July next year

The matter of Sino-British telegraph communication has been widely publicized for a long time. At present, the International Telecommunication Bureau is working hard to carry it out, and on the 20th of last month, it signed a communication contract with the Ministry of Communications and the British Imperial Communications Company. On the 28th of last month, it spent 780,000 yuan to purchase two short-wave generators from the British Marconi Company. The generators are the latest type of beam transmitters, whose English name is "Beam." The electricity emitted from Shanghai is focused into a line and directed straight to London, without scattering to other places. The beam transmitters can be shipped from London to Shanghai by the end of this year, and will be installed by the end of June next year. Formal communication can begin in July.

Falsifying Rent Tickets Was Prosecuted and Punished 156

Residents in the Public Concession who try to evade municipal donations have recently increased significantly. The Bureau of Works can only take legal action. Wu Changfu of 25-26 Shanxi Road was prosecuted by the Bureau of Works' lawyer, Mr. Ru Baoyi, on behalf of the police, in the Special District Court for falsifying rent tickets and not paying the full amount of the donation. In May of this year, the Donation Office found that the rent at that location, including water, was actually 137.5 yuan per month, so it calculated the donation amount based on 131 yuan. However, the defendant claimed that the monthly rent was 89 yuan and produced a rent ticket as proof. After investigation, it was found that the ticket was forged. Therefore, the Bureau of Works prosecuted him. After interrogation by the judge, the Donation Office stated the situation of going to collect donations on May 17th as stated by Mr. Chadar. According to the defendant, he opened a shop in the house at 25-26 Shanxi Road. The owner of the house is an insurance company, but he rented it from a Cantonese named Huang at the end of March, but he does not know where he lives. Since March, the rent has been collected three times, but there are no receipts. Then he changed his statement, saying that he had only received it once in mid-April and forgot to record it in the account. He only asked his wife to do it for him. After paying the rent once, he heard that the house had changed hands. When the donation collector came on May 17th, the receipt taken out by his wife was actually wrong. According to the rent collector of Qingyun Company, the company bought the house from Sassoon Yanghang in January of this year. The defendant also rented it in January. Before that, the rent was collected from a Cantonese. Since February, March, April, and May, the rent has been collected from the defendant, and the rent has not increased. It has always been 137.5 yuan. After the judge reviewed the case, he believed that the defendant should not have tried to forge documents and obtain improper benefits. He was fined 200 yuan or imprisoned for 100 days to show an example.

Twenty-One Ship Registration Offices Established 162

Since He Hanlan took over the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau, he has been carrying out rectification. He has abolished the offices and added 21 ship registration offices, which have now been established. The details are as follows:

Abolish offices The Maritime Affairs Bureau had 13 offices set up by the former director Xi Dingmo in Su, Wu, Zhen, and Wen ports. Due to financial constraints, six offices were canceled in April of this year, leaving seven offices to manage ship registration matters. After Director He took over, the offices in Su, Wu, Zhen, Wen, Zhakou, and Haizhou were also abolished to save expenses. The 13 offices were completely abolished.

Establish registration offices Director He established registration offices for ship registration in various places. After field investigation, it was decided to set up a total of 21 offices, of which seven are A-level. Six offices have been established first, and commissioners have been appointed. They are Xu Worru, Commissioner of Wuhu, Guo, Commissioner of Suzhou, Tan Boqiao, Commissioner of Zhenjiang, Xi Wu, Commissioner of Wenzhou, He Hao, Commissioner of Zhenhai, Tang Youlie, Commissioner of Zhakou, and Jiang Xintian, Commissioner of Haizhou. The B-level offices are Wang Hongjun, Commissioner of Wuxi, Dong Wei, Commissioner of Yuncang, He Shaoting, Commissioner of Sanhe, Pan Shenyong, Commissioner of Nan, Zheng Tihe, Commissioner of Huayang, Chen Shaofan, Commissioner of Dalier, Wang Bozhou, Commissioner of Shierwei, Zhou Yulin, Commissioner of Qingjiangpu, Weng Qibin, Commissioner of Jiaxing, Pan Guancao, Commissioner of Wuxing, and Zhang Guirong, Commissioner of Taizhou.

Preparations for three branch offices The three places of Wusong, Suzhou River, and Minhang have the most ship traffic. Director He also ordered the addition of three registration offices and appointed to be responsible for preparing the Wusong Registration Office. Jin Shisheng and Lin Siduan were appointed to handle the registration matters in the Suzhou River and Minhang areas. Wusong is classified as A-level, and Suzhou River and Minhang are classified as B-level. The organization of the registration office is composed of commissioners, technicians, clerks, and section members, who specialize in registration and fee collection.

Shanghai's Central Fei Huaitang Wrongfully Died, Coffin Opened for Inspection 163

Fei Huitang from Xuzhou, 38 years old, had been running a tobacco and paper shop in Guanyintang, Tanjia, Hutai Road, Zhabei. When the Shanghai war broke out, Fei refused to flee and remained in the area. When our army retreated to the second line of defense, the area fell to the enemy. As a result, traitors took the opportunity to rise up and often formed gangs to rob and plunder. How could the Fei family be spared? On March 29th, many people suddenly came to Fei's shop with guns to search and loot. Everything, big and small, was tied up and taken away. Fei's life was tied to this, and he died of resentment. His family did not dare to speak out and hastily collected the body. Now that the situation has calmed down, Fei's brother, Fei Futang, believes that his brother died tragically and filed a complaint with the local court requesting redress. The court ordered that the coffin be brought to the court for inspection. Yesterday, the coffin was brought to the forensic inspection office. The village prosecutor and inspectors Shen and Xuan came to the office to inspect the body. It was found that the body had already turned to ashes, leaving only bones. It was confirmed that there was a gunshot wound under the skull. After filling out the inspection report, the court ordered the arrest of the murderer. The coffin was ordered to be taken away.

Farmers Struck by Lightning in Western Shanghai 164

Yu Fuquan, the son of Yu Guiqing, a farmer residing at No. 7 Yujia East House, Meiyun Town, Western Shanghai, was 34 years old. At 6:00 p.m. the day before yesterday (the 10th), Yu was irrigating fertilizer in the field when suddenly dark clouds gathered and it began to rain heavily. Lightning flashed and Yu tried to escape, but was struck by lightning in the field. Two other people, A and B, were also working at the same time and were close to Yu. They were greatly shocked and notified Yu Guiqing to come and see. He saw that the deceased had no injuries, but there were some faint black spots like fire burns on his body. More than half of his hair had been burned. Yesterday, Gui reported to the Sixth District Third Branch and requested exemption from inspection. He has now collected the body himself.

Suicide Due to Economic Distress 165

Zhou, a 41-year-old man from Nanjing who lived on Gordon Road, had been unemployed for three years. He had a wife and several children who all depended on him for a living. Therefore, his economy has recently become more strained, and he has pawned almost everything. He failed to borrow money from a friend the day before yesterday, which caused him to feel deeply resentful. Finding no way out, he conceived the idea of ​​being tired of the world and secretly bought opium to swallow and commit suicide to end his remaining life. His wife, Li, noticed and accompanied him to the Labor Hospital. Because he was deeply poisoned, there was no way to rescue him and he soon died. The body was taken to the corpse inspection office on Fellen Road. Yesterday morning, Inspector Li was commissioned by the First Special District Local Court to go to the office to confirm the death. He sat on the case and questioned Li, Zhou's wife. He ruled that Zhou Shuyuan had died of opium poisoning and ordered his wife, Li, to sign a statement and claim the body for burial.

Arrest of Twelve Male and Female Thieves, Confiscation of Handguns and Bullets 166

The Thieves Confessed Readily to Robbery

Woman Named Meiyu Granted Bail

The home of Madam Zhou Shi, located at No. 4, Lane 132, Route d'Edoard, was burglarized on the 13th of last month by five or six bandits who brandished handguns, silencing any outcry, and making off with valuables worth over 1,500 yuan. Afterward, Madam Zhou reported the incident to the Zhabei Police Station, requesting an investigation. Detectives Zhao Fuhai and Cui Shun of the station learned that the bandits were planning another robbery on the night of the 9th at 10:30 PM, and would pass through the intersection of Route d'Edoard and Yunnan Road. They coordinated with Inspectors Tang Jian and Li Shizhong, and Detective Ye Yushan, and proceeded to the location to lie in wait. When Liang Guisheng, Wu Xiaoming, Liu Qianbao, and Chen Rongsheng arrived, the detectives apprehended them together at the station. Upon interrogation, it was learned that other accomplices were hiding in various locations. The detectives then went to No. 44, Yong'an Li, Yunnan Road, Room 38 of the Great Shanghai Hotel, and No. 12, Route Amiral Courbet, where they successively apprehended Shi Baosheng, Ren Zixin, Lin Tiansheng, Dong Shengjing, Shen Pengfei, Zhu Shuangxi (also known as Wang Kunshan), as well as a woman named Xiao Meiyu and a woman named Ding Zhangshi. They also confiscated five handguns, thirty-five bullets, and pawn tickets for jewelry. Xiao Meiyu was a performer of "civilized drama" at the Tianyun Building of the Wing On Company and had been involved with Lin Tiansheng for some time. Yesterday morning, the police station summoned the victim, Madam Zhou Shi, and transferred the male and female bandits to the First Special District Court, where Judge Ge interrogated them. According to the police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, the other individuals involved had not been investigated thoroughly for other robbery cases, so the charges were only for illegal possession of military firearms and artillery. He requested an extension of the investigation after the hearing to facilitate further investigation. However, Xiao Meiyu had been cooperative with the police in the investigation, and he requested that she be granted bail pending trial. Madam Zhou Shi then identified Liang Guisheng, Lin Tiansheng, and Dong Shengjing as having been present at her home during the robbery. The three thieves confessed to the robbery upon hearing the victim's testimony. Shen Pengfei was even more forthcoming, readily admitting that he had also participated in the robbery at Madam Zhou Shi's home, and offered that two of the five handguns seized were his. Dong also confessed that the other three handguns belonged to him. The judge then granted Xiao Meiyu bail, ordering her to be available for questioning upon notice, and remanded the rest to custody, postponing the hearing for fourteen days.

On June 25th, at Li Yuanhe Tobacco and Paper Shop, No. 181, Sanguantang Road, they robbed 20,000 copper coins. Jin Bohe fired a shot, but he didn't know if anyone was injured. Wu Si, also known as Wu Jinyu, age 34, from Yancheng, confessed that he had participated in the robberies of Xinyuanzhen, Qin Siyi's home, and Li Yuanhe Tobacco and Paper Shop, and received a total of 24 yuan as his share. Zang Dacai confessed that he had robbed Longmao Tobacco Shop at No. 289, Meixie Road, on May 12th, Yuan Changrong's water boiler shop at No. 351, Guohuo Road, on May 27th, Xinyuanzhen Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 109, Xihua Li, Xiejiao, in early June, Qin Siyi's home at No. 185, Longhua Road, on June 12th, and Li Yuanhe Tobacco and Paper Shop at No. 181, Sanguantang Road, on June 25th. In each robbery, they used a handgun owned by Jin Bohe. The women, Han Pengshi and Wu Lishi, claimed they were unaware of the robberies. Xue Man, who worked as a stoker at the water boiler shop in Fuxing Li, Xie Xu Road, said that police officers had arrested him at the water boiler shop the previous night. He didn't recognize any of the robbers, but if they had come for tea, he wouldn't remember them because many people came for tea. After questioning the suspects, District Chief Zhang brought the victims to the district headquarters to confirm the robberies and provide a list of stolen items. Local News II

Second Public Hearing on Suspicious Death of Russian Beggar 168

Three Witnesses Deny Beating of Russian Beggar

Body Scheduled for Exhumation and Re-examination Tomorrow

The case of the suspicious death of Russian beggar Georgi Latych-Eff, who died in the Second Special District Court detention center on the 19th of last month, has been investigated by the Police Department. As a result, Warden Xu Chongwen, Medical Officer Yu Minggao, and Prison Worker Zhou Zongxiang have been charged with abandonment and assault in the Second District Court. Judge Wang Gangxu of the Criminal Division held a hearing and adjourned the case for a later date. Meanwhile, Judge Ying Shi and Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan have jointly sent a letter to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home, instructing them to transport the coffin to Shanghai for re-examination. This matter has already been reported in the newspapers. Here is the latest news:

Coffin Transported to Shanghai The coffin arrived at the Shanghai South Salvation Bureau at 7:00 AM yesterday and was immediately sent to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home. Mr. Qin Shounong, the former director of the funeral home, personally sealed the coffin with tape at the top, bottom, head, and feet. At 11:45 AM, the coffin was transported to the Bureau of Works autopsy room on Dallas Road and placed in a cold storage room to await the scheduled re-examination.

Individuals Present in Court Yesterday marked the second hearing in the case. The Police Department notified the plaintiffs and witnesses to be present for questioning. At 9:00 AM, the plaintiff, the deceased's brother, Simon Grietzki, and his lawyer, Plaimeh Eichenlin, arrived at the court to await the hearing. Witnesses Seriek Mutusnikoff (also translated as Kwatnitz-Gukoff), Dzipuk Dalaeff, and Vladimir Guruluk Tchirkina arrived shortly after. On the defendant's side, Medical Officer Yu Minggao and Prison Guard Zhou Zongxiang arrived. At 10:00 AM, Judge Wang, accompanied by Secretary Zhu, took their seats in Criminal Court No. 1. Judge Ying Shi also attended the hearing, sitting behind Judge Wang to listen. The Russian Emigrant's Association in China was represented by lawyer Wei, who also attended to listen.

Initial Questioning of the Plaintiff First, lawyer Feiduzhen from the Police Department stated that the Police Department had brought the plaintiff and all witnesses. The court ordered the plaintiff, the deceased's brother, to be brought to the stand for questioning (all words were translated by translator Shen Jinshun). He stated that his name was Simon Grietzki, age 35, a Russian national, residing at No. 108, Huanlong Road. The deceased, Georgi Latych-Eff, was his younger brother, age 33. Asked how he knew Georgi Latych-Eff was his brother, he replied that he had seen a photograph and had been told by others. Asked if he knew his brother had been arrested, he replied that he did not. Asked if he knew about his brother's death, he replied that he learned of it from someone who had been detained with his brother. Asked if he had seen the body after death, he replied that he had reported it to the police station but had not seen the body. The court then showed him a photograph and asked if the person was his brother, to which he replied yes. Asked how he knew his brother had been beaten to death as he reported at the police station, he replied that Seriek Mutusnikoff, who had been detained with him, had reported to him that his brother had been beaten to death by a prison guard, and that there were serious injuries to his head, face, nose, and chest. One account said that he died of illness but was not treated when he was sick. Asked if he wanted to request a re-examination of the body, he replied yes, he wanted to request a re-examination. Asked how long it had been since he last saw his brother, he replied that he had last seen him seven days before his arrest, at the evening newspaper office, where he worked as a proofreader. He also stated that his brother had no wife or children. Asked if he was willing to proceed even though the body had already decomposed and external injuries would be difficult to detect, he replied that he was.

First Witness At this point, the judge ordered the first witness to be questioned. Lawyer Plaimeh, representing the plaintiff, stated that he had a few important words to say before the witnesses were questioned and requested that the court question the two defendants (his intention was likely to prevent the defendants from hearing the witnesses' testimonies and changing their own). The judge asked if he was afraid that the defendants would hear the witnesses' words and then ordered defendants Yu and Zhou to leave the courtroom. The witness, Seriek Mutusnikoff, then stated that he was age 50, a Russian national, currently residing with friends at no fixed address, and made a living doing small business. The judge told the witness that he had to tell the truth and that, according to Chinese law, he had to swear an oath first, and that he could be charged with perjury if he lied. The witness agreed and signed the oath. Asked what his relationship was with the deceased, he replied that they were friends. Asked when he had met him, he replied that they had known each other for a year. Asked when he had arrived at the detention center, he replied that he had not arrived with the deceased and had been there one day earlier. Asked what he had been arrested for, he replied that he had been arrested on the street for allegedly violating regulations. Asked who had arrived at the detention center with Georgi Latych-Eff, he replied that Dzipuk Dalaeff and Vladimir had arrived with him. Asked if Georgi Latych-Eff had any injuries or marks when he arrived at the detention center, he replied that he had seen that he was sick and had blood in his nose, but the injuries were covered by blood, so he could not tell. Asked if he had asked him who had hit him, he replied that he had asked him, but he did not say. He could not stand and fell to the ground, only asking for water and not speaking. Asked who had hit him, he replied that he did not know how he had been hit and had not seen anyone hit him. Asked if anyone had hit him inside the detention center, he replied that he had not seen anyone hit him from the time he entered the detention center until his death, which was about 40 hours, but he had seen blood on his left face. Asked if he had been helped into the detention center by two people, he replied that he had been eating and sleeping at the time and had not seen it, but he had heard that he had been helped in. Asked if he was already sick when he entered the detention center, he replied that he was already sick when he entered. Asked if a doctor had treated him after he entered the detention center, he replied that he had not been treated. Asked if he had been given medicine to drink, he replied that he had only seen him drink water twice and had not seen any medicine. Asked what he looked like inside the detention center, he replied that he looked very uncomfortable and could only say a few words. Asked if his words were truthful, he replied that they were, and he swore an oath.

Second Witness The witness, Dzipuk Dalaeff, stated that he was 34 years old, a Russian national, working as a pastry chef, residing at No. 782, Avenue Joffre. The judge ordered him to swear an oath. Asked if he and Georgi Latych-Eff had been arrested at the same time on June 17th and why, he replied that they had been arrested for drunkenness. Asked if the deceased had been beaten by anyone before arriving at the court, he replied that he had not seen him beaten by anyone. Asked if the deceased was sick when he entered the detention center, he replied that he was already sick and was vomiting blood. Asked what his illness looked like, he replied that he was mildly ill when he was arrested but became more seriously ill after the arrest. He could not walk and had to be helped in by two people. Asked where the blood on his face came from, he replied that it came from his nose. Asked if the prison guard had hit him, he replied that he had not seen the prison guard hit him. Asked if the three of them had been detained in the same cell, he replied that they had been arrested together in Cell No. 4 and remained together until his death. Asked if a doctor had treated him in the detention center, he replied that they had asked the prison guard to call a doctor, but the prison guard said he would be treated the next day, but he never saw a doctor treat him before he died. Asked if he had been given medicine to drink, he replied that he had not been given any medicine and no doctor had come. Asked if anyone in the detention center had hit him, he replied that no one had ever hit him. Asked if his words were truthful, he replied that they were.

Third Witness The judge asked the witness, Vladimir Guruluk Tchirkina, if he was arrested with the deceased Georgi Latych-Eff. The witness replied that the matter was the same. The witness explained that the victim was arrested first, followed by the witness, but they were taken to court together. The witness was asked when they entered the detention center, and he responded that it was before dinner on June 17th. When asked if the deceased was ill upon entering the detention center, the witness answered affirmatively. Asked whether the deceased had blood on his face, the witness replied that his nose was injured and bleeding. When questioned about whether anyone had beaten the deceased inside the detention center, the witness stated that he had not seen anyone hit him. Asked if he and the deceased were in the same room, the witness confirmed they were. The witness was asked if they had told the guards about the deceased's illness, to which he replied that they had. Asked if a doctor had come to see him, the witness said no doctor had come. Asked if any medicine was given, the witness said no one had given any medicine. When asked about the nature of the deceased's illness, the witness replied that he was not a doctor and did not know. Asked about the symptoms in the detention center, the witness stated that the deceased could not eat and was vomiting. At this point, the judge addressed the plaintiff, stating that according to the witnesses, no one had beaten his brother in the detention center. The plaintiff responded that he had received a letter from Mutusnikoff and had been told in person at the church that someone had hit him. The plaintiff had invited him to report to the police station together the next day, but he did not come.

Defendant Testimony The judge ordered the two defendants, Yu and Zhou, to be brought in. Zhou Zongxiang was asked if the three Russians testifying were in Cell No. 4 at the time. Zhou examined the faces of the three men and replied that the first two were, but he did not remember the third. Zhou was asked if they had asked him to call a doctor, and he replied that they had not. He stated that it was after 5 o'clock, which was dinnertime, and the deceased was lying on the ground, not eating. He reported this to the warden and asked the medical officer to come and treat him. The judge then asked the three Russian witnesses if they recognized the defendant, medical officer Yu Minggao. They all said they had never seen him before. Yu was asked if he had treated the deceased, and he replied that he had treated him. He stated that it was dinnertime and he was afraid they would be eating and not paying attention, but he went to see the patient. He did not speak to them and there was no need to speak to them. They did not recognize him, and he did not recognize them. He rarely went into the prison cells. The judge then asked the three Russians if they were eating and did not notice the medical officer coming to examine the patient. The three men all replied that they were together and had not seen the doctor come. He then asked Zhou if he had been eating in the cell when the meal was served. He replied that they were eating in the cell. The plaintiff's lawyer, Plameh, asked the court to ask medical officer Yu Minggao what clothes the deceased was wearing when he examined him. Yu replied that he was wearing ordinary clothes. The judge then asked the three Russians what color clothes the deceased was wearing. They all replied that he was wearing black wool. The Police Department's lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stated that he had a question for medical officer Yu: Did he go to treat patients in the detention center based on a report from the prison guard, or did he need permission from the warden to enter the detention center to treat patients? Yu replied that he would naturally need to obey the warden's orders and have permission to enter the detention center to treat patients. Otherwise, he could not directly enter the prison cell. The judge then asked the plaintiff, the deceased's brother, if he insisted on requesting a re-examination of the body. The plaintiff replied that he wanted a clear re-examination to determine the cause of death.

Exhumation Tomorrow At this point, it was noon. The court clerk stood up and read aloud the transcripts of each person's testimony. The court then decided to exhume and re-examine or dissect the body of Georgi Latych-Eff at 10:00 AM on the 13th to conduct further inquiries. The court then adjourned.

Shipping Dispute Caused by Yu'an's Chartered Boat Attracts Attention from Shipping Industry 169

Arbitration Cannot Cancel Contract

Both Parties Involved in Legal Remedies

The Yu'an Shipping Company in this city chartered the Taiping ship from Zhongwei to load goods in North China. After the outbreak of the Shanghai war, Yu'an wanted to recover the charter fee. Zhongwei refused the request because it was not in accordance with the facts and principles. Yu'an then submitted to arbitration. However, Yu'an overturned the arbitration award and filed a lawsuit, which has caused resentment in the Shanghai shipping industry. They are afraid that opening this unreasonable dispute will have a huge impact on the shipping industry and will lead to various disputes. Now Zhongwei has also filed a counterclaim, which is detailed below.

Chartering Before the War The Yu'an Shipping Company chartered the Taiping ship from Zhongwei Company because a large number of coal was loaded from Tianjin to various parts of Guangdong. The monthly rent should have been 15,000 yuan. Due to the friendship between Chen Shuntong and Zhao Yuntai, the rent was reduced to 13,500 yuan. The Taiping ship was chartered to Tianjin, and the Shanghai war had not yet broken out. When it arrived in North China to transport goods, the war in Shanghai had already broken out. However, at this time, coastal merchant ships were still operating normally, and those in the North and Guangdong were even less affected. However, Zhao Yuntai suddenly proposed to terminate the contract with Zhongwei.

Dispute over Suspension of Rent The Yu'an Company used the excuse of the Sino-Japanese war to terminate the charter and asked Zhongwei to refund the fee. Zhongwei Company believes that Yu'an has misinterpreted the provisions and does not conform to the facts and principles of the Shanghai war. How can they use this to distort the facts? Moreover, the Taiping ship chartered to travel from the North to Guangzhou is not within the Shanghai war zone. The ship has not been affected in practice, so it cannot overturn the contract and create this bad precedent.

Shipping Association Arbitration Zhao Yuntai, the owner of Yu'an, submitted the dispute to the Shanghai Shipping Association for arbitration. The Shipping Association designated Chen Ganqing, the owner of Zhao Xing Shipping Company, and Wang Bofen, the manager of Zheng Ji Shipping Company, as arbitrators. After several meetings, the arbitration plan was as follows: (1) Although the war broke out in Shanghai, war had not been formally declared, and commercial ships were not hindered. Moreover, the stevedores at the wharves in this city had not stopped unloading goods. The charter contract should not be cancelled. (2) The two companies are both members and should prioritize sentiment. The second month's rent that has already been paid should not be refunded, and the third month's rent will no longer be paid, thus ending the contract. The Tianjin-Guangdong line is even safer, and there is no reason to cancel the contract and demand a refund.

Filing a Lawsuit Zhao expressed dissatisfaction with the arbitration notice and proposed using the Englishman Maller as an arbitrator again. The result was the same as above, ordering the third month's rent to be stopped. Zhao was also dissatisfied and asked a lawyer to use the excuse of the war to overwhelm Zhongwei, so as to achieve the purpose of terminating the contract and returning the charter fee, but this has caused dissatisfaction in the Shanghai shipping industry.

Zhongwei Counterclaims After this incident, most of the shipping companies in this city advocated ending the case in accordance with the arbitration. However, after Zhao Yuntai filed a lawsuit, it was tantamount to considering the arbitrators' claims to be illegal, which aroused resentment in the shipping industry. The reason is that the Taiping ship did not travel in the war zone, but transported goods on a safe route, without suffering any loss. Moreover, the contract clauses contain legal principles. The Japanese did not declare war and these points cannot distort the clauses. If other ships follow this precedent and refuse to recognize the charter fee, wouldn't it affect the whole situation with one move and create a bad precedent? Today, Zhongwei Company has submitted various evidence to its hired lawyer to prepare to file a counterclaim.

Hardoon Estate Case Ruled in Favor of Hardoon's Wife 170

British Court Made Ruling the Day Before Yesterday

Following repeated court hearings held by the British Court of Probate in the past month regarding the Hardoon estate case, the presiding judge, Glan, delivered a verdict yesterday morning (the 10th), upholding Hardoon's will. The plaintiff lost the case, and all four million pounds of the estate remain under the control of Hardoon's wife.

Arguments in the Estate Dispute After the Jewish tycoon Hardoon passed away on February 1st of last year, his will stipulated that all his assets be given to his wife, Mrs. Luo Jialing. On July 16th, the British Court of Probate examined and approved the will. However, two months later, a person named Ezra Hardoon, claiming to be a cousin of the deceased Hardoon, filed a petition with the British Court of Probate to halt the legal proceedings. At the same time, he submitted a sworn affidavit stating that the deceased was mentally incapacitated when the will was signed and was subject to undue influence, rendering the will invalid. On November 9th, Ezra Hardoon appeared in court again and supplemented his reasons, stating that the estate should be handled in accordance with Iraqi law. On December 1st, he submitted a further complaint, claiming that the deceased was a Jew born in Baghdad and was under the protection of British diplomats according to the 1924 Anglo-Iraqi Treaty. Therefore, the deceased was not British. Jewish customs do not recognize marriage between Jews and non-Jews. According to Iraqi law, the will can only include one-third of the deceased's property, and foreigners cannot inherit the estate.

Hardoon's Wife's Defense The defendant, Mrs. Hardoon, admitted that the deceased Hardoon was a Jew born in Baghdad but denied that he was only under the protection of British diplomats because of the Anglo-Iraqi Treaty. She claimed that she had obtained British nationality, was legally married, and had long abandoned her original domicile and obtained a domicile in China. She also denied that the plaintiff and the deceased were cousins.

Another Hardoon Joins the Estate Dispute The case was heard by Sir Glan, the British Consul General, on June 6th. The plaintiff was represented by lawyers Wilkinson and Brownell, while the defendant was represented by lawyers Potter from Hong Kong and Brandt from Shanghai. After the trial began, another Hardoon from Mumbai, Isaac Hardoon, also claiming to be a close relative of the deceased, joined the lawsuit, represented by lawyer Samuel from London and lawyer Haddad from Shanghai. After two weeks of hearings, the trial was concluded.

Key Points of the Verdict Yesterday morning, the British Consul General announced the verdict, ruling in favor of the defendant. The verdict stated that anyone under British protection is in the same position as British citizens in terms of jurisdiction and law. Furthermore, the deceased Hardoon had obtained a domicile in China, and his estate should be handled according to the laws of the country of residence. According to the Sino-British Treaty, the case is under the jurisdiction of the British court, and the laws followed by the British court are naturally British law. The verdict also stated that if the case were appealed, the Iraqi law and Jewish law mentioned in the case were not proven during the trial. Furthermore, the plaintiff did not provide any evidence to prove that Ezra Hardoon and the deceased were cousins. As for Isaac Hardoon's claim that he was a close relative of the deceased, it was only based on what his deceased father, who died 44 years ago, had told him. The verdict also stated that the will was properly signed by the deceased and the witnesses and was indisputable. The claim that the deceased was mentally incapacitated had been abandoned. After the verdict was announced, the defendant's lawyer requested a one-month stay of execution, which was not granted by the court. The two parties' lawyers then jointly requested that the court fees be apportioned according to a specific form.

Snake and Hedgehog Fight 171

Spectators Marvel

Thief Seizes Opportunity to Steal

A rogue from Zhenjiang named Wang Zigui recently obtained a small green snake and a hedgehog (commonly known as a "melon-stealing beast") in the countryside. He trained the two creatures to fight, and then drew crowds to watch in open spaces. He colluded with accomplices Da Shunzi and Da Xingzi, who took the opportunity to steal valuables from the spectators. Their success rate was high, and they divided the spoils for their own use. The number of victims was countless. At around 8 a.m. the day before yesterday, they were again performing near the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Wuchang Road, attracting a large crowd. A Jiangxi man named Ding Amao was also watching and marveling at the spectacle when he suddenly discovered that his wallet, containing 27.20 silver dollars, had disappeared. He shouted for the thief to be caught. Detective Bai Mingfu happened to be investigating the area and, after learning the details, arrested Wang and took him to the police station. However, his accomplices had already escaped. Yesterday, he was handed over to the First Special District Court, where Judge Shen Bingrong planned to try him. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin explained the details of the case and requested that the defendant be punished as a warning to others. The judge questioned the defendant and, after clarifying the facts, sentenced the defendant to one year of imprisonment as a warning. The bamboo cage used to store the snake and hedgehog was confiscated.

Adulterer Convicted of Wounding Husband 172

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

A woman from Yangzhou named Huang Zhangshi, aged twenty-four, residing at No. 2 Tao Peng Road, recently formed an illicit relationship with Wang Jinsheng from Qingjiang. They engaged in clandestine affairs more than once. Her husband, Huang Jialin, was completely unaware. One evening at half-past ten, Wang Jinsheng took advantage of her husband being out enjoying the cool air, stealthily entered her bedroom, intending to continue their affair. While they were sitting on the bed whispering sweet nothings, her husband Huang Jialin returned home and witnessed the scene. Filled with anger, he grabbed a kitchen knife and violently struck Wang Jinsheng in the head, causing injury. Wang, being very strong, still attempted to escape through the door, and in turn, seized the knife, slashing Huang Jialin's left wrist. They wrestled to the ground. Patrolman Li Wenzhao discovered them and apprehended Wang Jinsheng, taking him to the police station. The police chief, after questioning them, found that both had been injured and ordered them to be sent to Tongren Hospital. Fortunately, their injuries were minor. After the doctor applied medication and bandages, they were immediately discharged. Yesterday morning, the police station escorted Wang Jinsheng to the First Special District Court for investigation. Subsequently, the plaintiff testified about the situation at the time. Huang Zhangshi also confessed that she had known the defendant privately for only two or three months. Last night, he came again, intending to continue their affair, and the conflict arose when her husband returned home. The court reprimanded her for her shamelessness and ordered her to leave. Then, Huang Wangshi, the woman’s mother-in-law, testified that the defendant indeed entered her daughter-in-law’s room and engaged in lewd behavior. This was seen by Jialin, leading to a jealous uproar, and he was instead wounded by the knife. When questioned, the defendant claimed that he had known the plaintiff for a long time and had previously asked him to introduce business. He was borrowed five yuan, and last night he went to collect the debt. He accused me of having an affair with the woman, and he used a kitchen knife to cut my head, so I seized the knife and cut his wrist, which is the truth. Judge Shen Bingrong ordered the court attendants to accompany both the plaintiff and defendant to the forensic doctor for examination. Wang Jinsheng was then sentenced to imprisonment for months as a warning.

Female Painter Accuses of Fraudulent Marriage 173

Combined with Bigamy Case for Trial

Guo Luman, son of wealthy merchant Guo Yonglan, recently held a wedding ceremony with female painter Xu Zhiqing, leading Guo's legal wife, Guo Han, nee Han Yueling, to accuse Guo of bigamy to the police. Special Article

When Will the Conversion from Tael to Yuan Happen? (Continued) 188

Jiang Lizhao

(3) The Paper Dock Problem. This is a concern of the Qian industry, in light of the disastrous precedents of the ruble, mark, and the domestic warlord's abuse of paper money. Their concerns are well-intentioned, and we should not criticize them too harshly. Moreover, no one can guarantee that such situations will not recur in the future. However, history shows that the trend of economic evolution will inevitably lead to an era of credit, which is unavoidable. If we are afraid to use banknotes after seeing the previous failures, and even unwilling to switch to the silver yuan represented by banknotes, we would not only be acting out of fear of choking, but also be making something practically impossible. For example, when riding a car, if a car crashes, the focus should be on improving driving skills, not abandoning cars altogether. Therefore, if we want to prevent the abuse of banknotes after the conversion to yuan, we should study the system of issuance, how to maintain credibility and prevent abuse, and how to supervise the government and banknote issuers to avoid the dangers of a paper dock. This is the fundamental solution.

Moreover, if banknotes can be abused after the conversion to yuan, can't Zhuang bills be abused before the conversion? Because it is a credit tool, and to say that banknotes representing silver yuan are prone to , while Zhuang bills representing silver taels must have sufficient cash reserves, is also untenable. Here are excerpts from Mr. Geng Aide's survey of the number of banknotes issued in Shanghai and the warehouse receipts of Chinese and foreign silver firms, listed in the table below for proof. (Large silver can also be minted into coins, so it is not included.)

Year | Silver in Reserve | Yuan in Reserve | Banknotes Issued

End of 1926 | 70,570,000 | 68,980,000 |

Total Silver and Yuan | Total Amount | Silver Stored by Chinese Banks

Assuming 7.2 mace equals one yuan, the average percentage of silver and yuan, Chinese banks account for 69.32%, and foreign banks account for 30.68%. Based on the above statistics, there are several points to note. (1) The inventory of silver taels in Shanghai's Chinese and foreign banks is decreasing, while silver yuan is increasing rapidly. (2) For the average inventory of silver and yuan, Chinese banks account for 69.32%,

. Foreign banks account for 30.68%. (3) Chinese banks hold more silver yuan, accounting for 85.63%, while foreign banks hold more silver taels, accounting for 62.83%. (4) At the end of the 19th year, the amount of banknotes issued was 271,000,000, and the silver yuan in reserve was 177,510,000. Even considering only Chinese banks and firms, there was a huge sum of 155,900,000 as of October 14th. It must also be explained that the banknotes of various Chinese banks are mostly circulating in the interior. For example, the Central Bank's banknotes represent the entire amount issued. The China Communications Bank also represents the total amount issued in several southeastern provinces, while the reserves only refer to those in Shanghai. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Discussion

The Truth After Suicide 191

--- Buddha

Recently, China's national crisis has become increasingly urgent, and livelihoods have become increasingly difficult. Suicide incidents are frequently heard of. Resident Hongye, with the ambition to lament the world and pity the people, wrote the book (The Truth After Suicide) to persuade everyone. Based on scientific theory and citing abundant examples, every word is pertinent and can be called a masterpiece. If you wish to request a copy, please attach a one-cent postage stamp and ask the Nanjing Middle School Tutorial Department to obtain it.

Because of this book, I can't help but have a feeling about today's youth. The youth of our country today do indeed feel troubled, pained, and without a way out. However, this situation is not only true for the youth of our country, but also for the youth of other countries. Especially in China, where economic production is backward, that goes without saying. However, when examining the reasons for youth suicide recently, there are no more than two paths: one is economic oppression, and the other is love problems. Because the thinking of the general youth of today is very wrong, believing that life only counts as not being troubled and as having a way out if one lives in a Western-style house, rides in a car, and embraces a modern girl. This is a big mistake.

In the world today, to be a person, to beg for food is right, to be a coolie is right, to eat vegetable roots and live in small houses is right. Living in a Western-style house and riding in a car is originally an exception. The road that a person comes from out of hardship and difficulty is called a way of life. The road that is found with one's brains and energy is counted as a way of life. To sit on a family fortune or enjoy an existing business and eat comfortably is not called a way of life, it is called good fortune, it is called relying on blessings. Even in the past it was like this. There is an old saying (A great man can bend and stretch,) If one can only stretch and cannot bend, then one cannot be considered a great man. Look at the heroes of various countries, which one did not come out of struggle? If one were to seek a short life at the first setback, that is truly what women used to do, and what women today do not do. There is another old saying, (It is better to live badly than to die well) In fact, living badly is not very meaningful, because I was born a person, originally not only to consume bread, but to suffer hardships, and only after suffering hardships is there a way of life, but to find a way of life, one must first learn skills. If one does not learn skills and waits for happiness to descend, that is called abandoning oneself, and it is not a way of life.

As for committing suicide for love problems, it is even more of a joke. Love is originally a chance encounter. If you meet A today, you will fall in love with A. If you meet B today, you will fall in love with B. Is it possible that you will never fall in love with anyone if you don't meet A? Moreover, love is something that is active, changeable, and transferable. Therefore, the word love is not a problem in the first place. Not to mention that China is a country with no resources, even in the East and West, when it comes to marriage, one must be around thirty years old, which fits the ancient saying that at thirty one is strong and has a room. However, the ancients advocated late marriage from a physiological point of view, while foreigners advocate late marriage from a production point of view, because a perfect family requires a perfect economy to maintain. If you do not have the ability to produce, even if you have a modern girl, you will not only not get the happiness of love, but you will first suffer the pain of love. Conversely, if you have the ability to live, would you be afraid of not having a young and beautiful modern girl to accommodate you? If there is an inheritance left by your ancestors, that is an exception. If you are a young man who has no inheritance left by his ancestors, you should still try to study hard and enrich your tools for making a living, first find a bright and upright way out, and then slowly talk about love.

These words are not nonsense in front of you, I am also a person who is very qualified to commit suicide, I lost my education early, had a dictatorial marriage, and had no family property, so the conditions for suicide are all present, but now I am over fifty years old, and I am still struggling in the world. Not to mention suicide, even if Yama comes with a post to invite me, I will still fight him!

Science

Fire Liquor 194

— Lü Shuang

Fire liquor is the common name for methanol and ethanol, which are the most common of the monohydric alcohols. They have wide applications in industry, daily use, and medicine. Therefore, we will now discuss their manufacturing methods, properties, and so on:

(1) Methanol (CH2OH), also known as wood alcohol, is mostly obtained by dry distillation of wood in a vacuum under high heat. The distillate also contains acetic acid and tar. The tar can be removed by redistillation. Acetic acid can be neutralized with lime to form insoluble calcium acetate. What remains is 8% to 9% methanol and water. The water can then be removed by fractional distillation to obtain more concentrated methanol.

Recently, Germans have used steam and coal heated in a vacuum to produce hydrogen and carbon monoxide (H2O + CH2 + CO). These two gases are then reacted using a catalyst and heating to 300-400 degrees Celsius to form methanol (CO2H2CH3OH). The methanol obtained by this method is cheap, but unfortunately, it is kept secret, and we cannot readily apply it yet. We still need to work hard ourselves!

Methanol is highly toxic, and drinking it can be life-threatening. Therefore, it can only be used in industry and other non-ingestible manufacturing.

(2) Ethanol (C2H3CH), also known as grain alcohol, is present in ordinary alcoholic beverages at a content of 15% to 50%. Its toxicity is less than that of methanol. The cheapest method of manufacturing it is to ferment starch into sugar, which is then fermented into ethanol. Making rice wine at home uses this method.

Ethanol can be drunk and has wider uses. Therefore, in countries with alcohol prohibition, in order to limit drinking, it is stipulated that ethanol must be mixed with methanol in order to be sold tax-free, otherwise it is subject to heavy taxes. Therefore, ethanol sold on the market contains one-tenth methanol. Obtaining pure ethanol is very expensive.

Some pharmacies often sell ethanol that has been mixed with methanol as pure ethanol. Purchasers who are unaware suffer greatly. To find out if methanol is present, pour half a test tube of wine into a test tube, and then slowly pour concentrated sulfuric acid along the tube wall, about one-third of the wine volume. The sulfuric acid will sink to the bottom of the tube. Then, gently add a few drops of ferric chloride solution. If methanol is present, there will be a purple ring between the wine and sulfuric acid layers, which is very obvious.

Now let's talk about the uses of fire liquor: In industry, fire liquor is used as a raw material for making various items and as a solvent for water-insoluble substances. Various fragrances are extracted using fire liquor. In medicine, it has wide applications. Tincture of iodine is an alcohol solution of iodine, and various tinctures are extracts of drugs in ethanol. The value of fire liquor is more expensive than gasoline, so it cannot be used as a common fuel, but can only be used in the home.

We Chinese use fire liquor more and more every day. Except for a few alcoholic beverages, most of it is supplied by foreign countries, which is very regrettable. The method of making alcohol is not very difficult, and it is hoped that large capitalists will do their best to promote its manufacture.

A Corner of Society

A Scene in a Doctor's Office 195

— Kang Shi

A feeling of injustice is always suppressed by the word "poverty." Being sick is the most painful thing, especially for poor people. Of course, they don't have money to get treatment. Because of this delay, it's unknown how many lives are wasted! Although many charitable halls that provide medical consultations and medicine have been established in Shanghai society, they rarely have good effects on serious illnesses. Therefore, most doctors with greater skills have no choice but to put on airs, or not put on airs, but their signs cannot become famous. This is also an unfortunate thing for the poor in Shanghai!

The following is a scene of a poor person seeking medical treatment:

In the registration room of a doctor's office, a middle-aged woman came in. Her sallow face clearly showed malnutrition. Her hair was disheveled, and her eyebrows were deeply furrowed. Her short black cloth jacket had seven or eight patches, clearly showing that she was being oppressed by poverty!

The woman held a child of about two years old in her arms, who was almost skin and bones from illness. The child was crying loudly, and the veins on his head were bulging high!

"Sir! Can the consultation fee be reduced a bit? Please have some compassion and save this child's life!" The woman said to the registrar, pointing to the child in her arms.

"That's not possible!" the registrar said, glaring.

"Here are sixty cents! I pawned a short jacket this morning. Please make it easier for me!" The woman pleaded with a bitter face.

"Go sit over there, and after he's done examining other patients, he'll examine your child." The registrar hesitated for a long time before replying coldly.

"How much is the registration fee?" one of the patients asked. "Two dollars and forty cents," the registrar replied with a smile, very politely.

Only after several hours did the woman's child get examined. [The last one.] During these few hours, the woman saw how quick the registration was for others, while she [the last one] was met with several cold faces. How sad she was in her heart! However: A feeling of injustice is always suppressed by the word "poverty!"

School Writing

Joy and Sorrow 196

— Wu

The XX Conservatory of Music is holding a recital tomorrow. Miss Ye is a top student at the school and has been chosen by the school authorities as a performer and is in charge of the (piano solo) program.

Indeed, she plays the piano very well. For example, she has already mastered (Sonata) and other relatively common pieces. Even Beethoven's (Moonlight Sonata) she was able to play a long time ago. She is preparing to show off this famous piece at the recital tomorrow, so in recent days, she has hardly dared to leave the piano.

Now she plays it again and again. Every time she thinks of the unparalleled honor she will inevitably receive tomorrow, she feels immense joy in her heart.

"(Miss Ye!)" This is a classmate's call. "(Your newly made dress has arrived, come and try it on)." So she hurried back to her room.

The long, floor-length black dress, worn on her petite body, is indeed very moving from behind, but the brown spots all over her face and her large, thick, protruding lips reflected in the mirror make even herself feel ashamed. However, she believes that if she uses miraculous makeup techniques, it can definitely be concealed. For example, first apply a thick layer of white powder, and then use (Xi Shi powder) to draw appropriately on the lips, and even paint the eye sockets gray-brown, wouldn't it be possible to get by if you look at it from a distance? So she still feels joy.

Suddenly, a janitor came and said that the head of the piano department had called her to speak. When she walked into the faculty office, several classmates were already there. She walked up to the teacher, only to see the former Royal Academy of Music professor, a stateless White Russian with a full beard, cast a fierce glance over her, then shrugged his shoulders and frowned. After a long pause, the Royal Professor asked in a commanding tone:

"(Have you prepared your program for tomorrow?)"

"(I think I can handle it.)" She replied with confidence.

"(Humph?········)" He glanced at her again. Again, he shrugged his shoulders. His lips moved several times but no sound came out. Finally, he said decisively:

"(I think you don't need to attend tomorrow.)"

"(Ah! Why?)"

"(For no reason.······No, you will know yourself.)"

A wave of shame and anger swept over her heart, and she could still hear the snickers of her classmates in her ears. She retreated from the room dejectedly, overwhelmed with immense sorrow.

The next day she began to realize (The aristocratic professor is like this after all!)

Zheng Zeren v. Wang Yuanlong et al. for delivery of films and compensation (Main text): Defendant Wang Yuanlong shall deliver the two films "Heroes of the North" and "Three镖客" to the plaintiff and compensate for losses of 300 yuan. If the films cannot be delivered, the deposit of 2,134.60 yuan shall be returned. Huang Zhiqing is liable for subsidiary compensation if Wang Yuanlong is unable to pay the loss fee of 100 yuan for the "Three鏢客" film and return the deposit of 2,134.60 yuan. The plaintiff's other claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff 2/6 and the defendant 4/6.

Shanghai United Insurance Co., Ltd. v. Chen Shuntong for debt (Main text): Defendant Chen Shuntong shall repay the plaintiff's insurance premium of 1,124 taels, 9 qian, 2 fen of silver and the repair fee of 13,576.67 Hong Kong dollars. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.

Liyi Real Estate Company v. Liu Yongkang for rent arrears and eviction (Main text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 165 yuan and is allowed to terminate the lease and return the leased house to the plaintiff. The flat roof built by the defendant in the open space behind Shendeli shall be demolished immediately. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.

Hehe Gongji v. Weng Diming for payment of rent and return of the house (Main text): The defendant shall pay the plaintiff rent of 251.8 yuan and return the house at No. 69, Hehefang, Avenue Joffre. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. This judgment on the return of the leased house may be enforced provisionally.

Criminal Judgments:

Police Station v. Zhu Maonan et al. for opium case (Main text): Zhu Maonan is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for providing a building for people to use opium substitutes for profit. Ding Baolong is sentenced to two months of imprisonment for repeated use of opium substitutes. Li Yunqing, Zhang Daosheng, Wang Aqi, Xing Zhengfu, Zhu Xiuying, Chen Jinbao, and Ye Hairu are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment for using opium substitutes. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at the rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Li Yunqing, Zhang Daosheng, Zhu Xiuying, and Ye Hairu are each granted a two-year reprieve. The smoking paraphernalia, etc. shall be confiscated as per the list.

Police Station v. Huang A'gen et al. for gambling case (Main text): Huang A'gen is fined 30 yuan for gambling with property. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the fine at the rate of one day for every two yuan. Chen A'bao, Zhu Xianglin, Ju Erlang, Huang Zhanglin, and Shen Changfa are each fined 5 yuan for gambling with property. If they are unable to pay the fine, they shall each be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The gambling money and gambling paraphernalia shall be confiscated as per the list.

Private prosecutor Gao Da v. Er Lianzi et al. for injury case (Main text): This case is not accepted.

Police Station v. La Bang et al. for gambling and fraud case (Main text): La Bang and Xieweisi are each fined 150 yuan for gambling with property. If they are unable to pay the fine, they shall each be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. Seven train cards and three chips shall be confiscated. The other parts of the lawsuit are innocent.

Police Station v. Wang Dabao et al. for opium case (Main text): Wang Dabao, Lu Jinrong, and Dong Shibao are each fined 50 yuan for possessing opium and opium smoking paraphernalia. If they are unable to pay the fine, they shall each be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the fine at the rate of one day for every two yuan. The opium bubbles and smoking paraphernalia shall be confiscated and destroyed as per the list. Lu Hairong is innocent.

Police Station v. Yang Yushan for theft case (Main text): Yang Yushan is sentenced to eight months of imprisonment for joint theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at the rate of two days for one day of imprisonment.

Police Station v. Xu Guanfang for theft case (Main text): Xu Guanfang is fined 60 yuan for continuous theft. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the fine at the rate of one day for every two yuan.

Police Station v. Wu A'wu for gambling case (Main text): Wu A'wu is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and fined 160 yuan for helping to gather people for gambling for profit. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at the rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. Four Huahui papers, two yuan and four jiao of foreign currency, and thirty-five copper coins shall be confiscated.

Police Station v. Jiang Dingchen for injury case (Main text): Jiang Dingchen is sentenced to thirty days of detention for helping to injure a person's body. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the term of detention at the rate of two days for one day of detention.

Police Station v. Zhu Genfu et al. for obstructing freedom case (Main text): Chen A'gen is fined 20 yuan for wandering around and causing trouble to shops for no reason. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be detained for one day for every one yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the fine at the rate of one day for every one yuan. Zhu Genfu, Lu A'gou, Zhu Hailin, and Zhang Wengui are all innocent.

Police Station v. Niu Dexiang for theft case (Main text): Niu Dexiang is sentenced to twenty days of detention for theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the term of detention at the rate of two days for one day of detention.

Police Station v. Fan Jinde et al. for gambling case (Main text): Fan Jinde is fined 30 yuan for gambling with property. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. Ding A'tu, Xu A'fu, Yue Jinming, Zhou Jusheng, Zhang Xiangjin, and Zhou Yitai are each fined 5 yuan for gambling with property. Two sets of Pai Gow, two sets of Mahjong, three decks of poker, four decks of cards, ten dice, eight branches of double corners, and 270 copper coins shall be confiscated.

Police Station v. Zhang A'mao for opium case (Main text): Zhang A'mao is fined 20 yuan for possessing opium smoking paraphernalia. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized shall be deducted from the fine at the rate of one day for every two yuan. One opium pipe, one opium lamp, and one opium needle shall be confiscated and destroyed.

Private prosecutor Chen Ruilan v. Xu Wenlian for injury case (Main text): This private prosecution is returned.

Private prosecutor Chen Ruilan v. Xu Wenxian for injury case (Main text): Xu Wenxian is innocent. The incidental civil lawsuit is dismissed.

Private prosecutor Zhou Wenkui v. Shao Xiaoyong for issuing bad checks and fraud case (Main text): Shao Xiaoyong is fined 60 yuan for knowingly issuing checks with amounts exceeding his balance. If he is unable to pay the fine, he shall be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. Shao Xiaoyong shall repay Zhou Wenkui 550 yuan. The other parts of the lawsuit are innocent.
